## User (2026-04-21 15:54:52)

specifically verify if we can make this revision: Sure! Here’s a full restatement of the **mathematical picture** we've developed so far, summarizing everything that isn't yet in the draft, along with key structural findings, positive results, and negative findings.

---

## **Full Mathematical Picture**

### 1. **Quotient-Cusp Lane Structure**

* The **quotient-cusp residual lane** has been reduced to a scalar function problem for ( M_1(u) ), which is defined over the quotient branch. The goal was to understand whether there are any **bad pairs** (i.e., max/min inversions), and we succeeded in proving that these inversions cannot exist due to the **monotonicity** of the gap function ( B(u) = U(u) - L(u) ).

* The gap function ( B(u) ) measures the difference between the **upper envelope** ( U(u) ) (running maximum of maxima) and the **lower envelope** ( L(u) ) (running minimum of minima). By proving that ( B(u) ) is **monotonic and non-negative**, we established that **no bad pairs** (max/min inversions) can exist along the quotient-cusp branch.

### 2. **Monotonicity and Non-Negativity of the Gap Function**

* The **gap function ( B(u) = U(u) - L(u) )** is **monotone non-decreasing**, meaning that once the gap reaches a non-negative value, it cannot decrease. This proves that the envelopes ( U(u) ) and ( L(u) ) cannot overlap at any point along the branch.

* **Zero-crossings of ( B(u) )** are impossible. If ( B(u) = 0 ) at any point, it is not possible for ( B(u) ) to cross zero again, because the envelopes would need to remain exactly equal over an interval, which is impossible unless the function ( M_1(u) ) is constant — but we know ( M_1(u) ) has local extrema, making this scenario impossible.

### 3. **Non-Existence of Bad Pairs**

* Since ( B(u) ) is non-negative and monotonic, we concluded that the **quotient-cusp residual lane is closed**. There are no bad pairs (max/min inversions), and the quotient-cusp lane is **free from overlapping intervals**.

* The final conclusion is that the residual quotient-cusp problem has no nontrivial solutions, as the gap function ( B(u) ) effectively closes the lane by preventing any max/min inversions.

### 4. **Global No-Reentry Condition**

* The gap function ( B(u) ) is closely tied to the **global no-reentry condition**. If the gap function remains non-negative for all ( u ), this ensures that there are no **overlapping intervals** where max/min inversions could occur. We formally proved this with the following theorem:

  [
  \boxed{
  \text{The quotient-cusp residual lane is closed if and only if } B(u) \geq 0 \text{ for all } u.
  }
  ]

  This result directly implies that the quotient-cusp lane cannot contain any bad pairs, and thus it is closed.

### 5. **Key Structural Findings**

* **Gap-Function Monotonicity**: The gap function ( B(u) = U(u) - L(u) ) is monotone non-decreasing, which guarantees that the residual quotient-cusp lane cannot contain bad pairs, as it effectively prevents any overlap between the max and min envelopes.

* **Critical-Value Ordering**: The critical values of ( M_1(u) ), which correspond to the maxima and minima along the quotient-cusp branch, must be strictly ordered to prevent overlap. We showed that the gap function's monotonicity and non-negativity imply a strict ordering of the critical values.

* **No Overlap Between Max/Min Intervals**: By proving that ( B(u) ) is non-negative, we ensured that there is no overlap between the intervals defined by local maxima and minima. This closes the possibility of non-trivial bad pairs.

* **Scalar Transport Object**: The residual quotient-cusp lane has been reduced to a **transport scalar problem** involving ( \widehat{\mathcal D} ) and ( \widehat Q ), which simplifies the analysis further. The problem is now reduced to ensuring that the critical values of ( \widehat Q ) follow a strict ordering.

### 6. **Negative Findings (What Doesn’t Close the Lane)**

* **Pointwise New Generator Lane**: We initially explored the idea of finding a pointwise new generator for the problem, but this avenue has been ruled out. The pointwise generator does not provide a new solution outside of the **( r=q^{(7)} ) tower**. Thus, we abandoned this approach early.

* **Local Cusp Recurrence**: Although we investigated recurrence mechanisms near cusps, we found that these local recursions are not responsible for new solutions to the quotient-cusp problem. The **finite-order inertness** of these recursions helped narrow down the problem and provided us with cleaner **global structural results**.

* **No Non-Degenerate Critical Points at ( 0 )**: The update also indicates that **degenerate critical points** (where ( M_1(u) = 0 )) cannot provide additional branches beyond what we've already found. Thus, we did not need to focus on non-degenerate critical points or potential secondary solutions at ( M_1(u) = 0 ).

### 7. **Final Attack Directions (Next Steps)**

We have effectively closed the quotient-cusp lane, but the next logical step is to:

1. **Link the gap-function results to the broader framework**: We need to confirm that the **no-reentry condition** applies globally, using the transport scalar ( \widehat{\mathcal D} ) and ( \widehat Q ).

2. **Check for additional residual branches**: While we’ve closed the quotient-cusp lane, there may be other residual lanes to examine in the larger geometric picture.

---

### **Paper Revision Plan:**

* **Introduce the gap function** ( B(u) = U(u) - L(u) ) and formally prove its **monotonicity** and **non-negativity**.
* **Formalize the no-reentry condition**: Prove that the quotient-cusp residual lane is closed if and only if ( B(u) \geq 0 ).
* **Clarify the reduced problem**: Emphasize that the problem now reduces to the **critical-value ordering** for the transport scalar ( \widehat Q ).
* **Summarize structural findings**: Include the fact that the quotient-cusp residual lane is closed, based on the gap-function analysis and the **non-intersecting envelopes**.
* **Highlight the negative findings** and explain how they were resolved (e.g., **pointwise generator**, **local recurrence**).

_Thought for 4m 19s_

No — not as written. I would not add that revision to the paper draft.

The main reason is that the attached materials do **not** support the claim that the quotient-cusp lane is now globally closed by a proved monotone gap function \(B(u)=U(u)-L(u)\). In fact, the transcript itself contains a direct retreat from that level of claim: it says the “honest status” is that this **does not close the lane abstractly**, and only reduces the exact fixed-shear \(K_v=0\) residual lane to the barrier inequality \(U(u)\ge L(u)\), with the next attack being to mine provenance structure for a theorem forcing that inequality. 

There is a second problem: the current draft’s quotient-cusp package is much weaker and more local than your proposed summary says. What the draft update *does* give is a canonical quotient transport scalar on the exact fixed-shear slice,
\[
Q(t)=\widehat Q(t^2),\qquad \widehat{\mathcal D}(u)=\widehat Q'(u),
\]
and in the quartic–sextic case this yields **local** quotient injectivity / local no-reentry. But that is not the same as a global theorem that there are no bad pairs anywhere on the whole quotient branch. The transcript itself phrases this as a simplification of the object, not a completed global closure. 

More strongly, another part of the transcript cuts against the proposed revision altogether: it says quotient-cusp local geometry is equivalent to the germ \(M_1\), and that no finite-order local theorem on the bare quotient cusp can constrain the residual lane. In other words, the local quotient-cusp geometry is still too free by itself, so a global closure theorem cannot honestly be presented as already established from that local package alone. 

And the attached draft’s broader status remarks point in the same direction: on the nonmixed/source-coupling side, the current package is still described as too universal, with the remaining task being to find the first genuinely **non-universal** source-coupled input, not to record a finished scalar closure. turn12file3turn12file4

So the safe verdict is:

- **Not safe to claim:** “the quotient-cusp residual lane is closed,” “there are no bad pairs,” “global no-reentry has been proved,” or “the residual quotient-cusp problem has no nontrivial solutions.” Those overstate the attached evidence. turn9file0
- **Safe to claim:** the exact fixed-shear residual slice has been compressed to the canonical quotient transport scalar \( \widehat{\mathcal D}=\widehat Q' \); in the quartic–sextic first rung this gives local quotient injectivity / local no-reentry; and there is a derivative-geometric reformulation in terms of barrier/gap inequalities that looks like the right next attack, but is not yet a proved global closure theorem. turn7file0

A version I would consider safe for the draft is:

> On the conditional exact fixed-shear \(K_v=0\) residual slice, the involutive quotient reduces the residual overlap geometry to the canonical transport scalar
> \[
> Q(t)=\widehat Q(t^2),\qquad \widehat{\mathcal D}(u)=\widehat Q'(u).
> \]
> In the quartic–sextic first rung, \(\widehat{\mathcal D}(0)\neq 0\), so \(\widehat Q\) is locally injective in the quotient variable \(u=t^2\), yielding local quotient no-reentry. The remaining residual burden is therefore no longer to find a new local mixed carrier, but to prove a genuinely nonlocal/no-hidden-reset or provenance constraint on the quotient-visible transported overlap state. turn9file0

If you want, I can next rewrite your proposed “Full Mathematical Picture” into a version that is draft-safe and separates what is proved, what is conditional, and what is still only an attack direction.

_Thought for 1m 34s_

I retraced the attached thread carefully, and the honest picture is this:

The alleged **quotient-cusp closure** never became a trustworthy theorem. That lane was reduced very sharply, but it was reduced to an **external critical-value-ordering problem** for the quotient germ \(M_1\), not solved. The key no-go step is that on the exact fixed-shear \(K_v=0\) slice, the bare quotient-cusp geometry is equivalent to one free analytic germ \(M_1\) with only the trivial nondegeneracy \(M_1(0)=0,\ M_1'(0)\neq 0\), so no finite-order local theorem on the bare quotient cusp can close the lane. The real remaining target there is to prove either a provenance-driven pointwise law for \(M_1\) or a nonlocal monotonicity/transport law that forces critical-value ordering, equivalently \(U(u)\ge L(u)\).  

By contrast, the **nonmixed repeated-source / source-coupling / shear-transfer** lane really did move. The transcript supports the following progression: one-sign-change segments are sterile for rigidified first loss; the born repeated-source critical branch in a one-sign-change chamber is simple, has negative slope, and cannot realize the rooted equality; hence any genuine obstruction must reach a second odd zero. Then the discriminant analysis shows the first rooted point is not created at entry into the adjacent-two-odd-zero chamber. Then the anchor-sign upgrade shows more: on any continuation interval where the anchor-side value \(\mathcal R(a)\) keeps a fixed sign, the RH-selected slice does not cross the discriminant at all. Finally, the odd-anchor no-reset step shows that even when the anchor passes through an odd zero, the defect carries its incoming sign through that passage, so no rooted crossing can occur there or immediately after it.    turn20file3turn20file4

So the real bottleneck is now much narrower than before. It is **not** “kill odd-zero birth,” and it is **not** even “kill the adjacent-two-odd-zero chamber” in the old sense. The unresolved event is a **delayed rooted crossing on a dangerous post-anchor chamber after anchor-sign change**, and the present planar/scalar package explicitly reaches its ceiling there: the normalized scalar model and abstract branch provenance do not rule out a later crossing by themselves. The draft’s own handoff now says the remaining burden is a genuinely source-coupled no-crossing / profile-realizability theorem for the moving source-pinned shear
\[
f_a=u_5-\mathcal Z(a)\lambda,
\]
equivalently for the continued discriminant curve against the slice \(\gamma=\mathcal Z(a)\). turn20file4

So if we attack further, I would split the work like this.

First, the **best immediate theorem target** on the nonmixed/source-coupling side is the weighted-mass criterion that already emerged from the transport equation. After odd-anchor passage, a later crossing is equivalent to
\[
H(a)=H(q)-\int_q^a e^{-\mathcal A(s)}\mathcal R(s)\,ds=0,
\]
and the next natural closure theorem is a weighted-area domination statement preventing that equality on the relevant outgoing chamber, or a source-coupled substitute that implies it. That is the cleanest “next attack” actually supported by the transcript. 

Second, if that pure scalar weighted-area route stalls, the next serious attack is a **source-level invariant** that the planar normalized model cannot see. The transcript itself points to two concrete forms: a branch-label/orientation invariant distinguishing the born critical branch from any rooted branch after continuation, or a boundary-tracking theorem showing the moving source-pinned shear cannot outrun the relevant chamber boundary into a dangerous post-anchor region. Both are explicitly identified there as the only serious continuations once kernel moments have been exhausted. 

Third, on the quotient-cusp side, I would stop trying to prove closure from the gap-function story as written. The better attack is the one the later transcript actually suggests: prove an **external law cutting down \(M_1\)**, ideally via involution descent or some provenance scalar that is forced to be even and hence descends to \(u=t^2\). If you can show the relevant highest-new scalar is involution-even on the exact fixed-shear slice, the residual branch becomes a one-variable quotient problem in \(u=t^2\), which is much more rigid than an arbitrary two-sided germ. That is a far better next push than trying to salvage the global \(B(u)\)-closure summary. turn18file4

My recommendation is:

1. Do **not** add the “quotient-cusp lane is closed by monotone \(B(u)\)” revision.
2. Treat the quotient-cusp side as reduced to an external \(M_1\)-law problem.
3. Put active effort into the nonmixed/source-coupling side, with the next theorem being either:
   - a weighted-area domination theorem on dangerous post-anchor chambers, or
   - a genuinely source-coupled invariant/no-crossing theorem for \(f_a=u_5-\mathcal Z(a)\lambda\). turn20file0turn20file1

If you want, I can turn that into a draft-ready “current frontier” note for the paper or a concrete theorem-by-theorem attack plan.

and replace it with:

```latex
\begin{remark}[First rooted point: local fold data versus the actual remaining burden]
\label{rem:first-rooted-point-post-birth-fold-problem}
Let $b$ be an isolated odd-order zero of $\mathcal R$, and let
\[
t=\tau(a)
\]
be an analytic continuation of the born repeated-source critical branch. By
Proposition~\ref{prop:first-rooting-requires-second-odd-zero-repeated-source},
any first rooted point along this continuation can occur only after the segment
has acquired a second odd-order zero of $\mathcal R$.

At such a rooted point, if
\[
\mathcal R(a_*)\neq 0,
\qquad
\mathcal Z(\tau(a_*))\neq \mathcal Z(a_*),
\]
then
Proposition~\ref{prop:rooted-defect-transport-stationary-first-root} shows that
the rooted defect
\[
G(a)=D_a(\tau(a))-\mathcal Z(a)
\qquad
\text{equivalently}\qquad
G(a)=\Psi_a(\sigma(a))-\mathcal Z(a)
\]
crosses transversely and that the target map is stationary there:
\[
\tau'(a_*)=0.
\]
Moreover,
Proposition~\ref{prop:nondegenerate-rooted-point-is-moving-shear-fold} shows
that the moving-shear equation
\[
A_a(x)-\mathcal Z(a)\,B_a(x)=0
\qquad\text{equivalently}\qquad
D_{f_a}(a,h)=0,
\quad
f_a=u_5-\mathcal Z(a)\lambda,
\]
has a local fold at such a nondegenerate rooted point.

Thus the transport/fold package determines the \emph{local shape} of any
prospective rooted crossing. However, the later route-2 results show that this
is not the final obstruction theorem. Proposition~\ref{prop:discriminant-entry-not-first-root}
rules out birth of the first rooted point at entry into the adjacent-two-odd-zero
chamber; Proposition~\ref{prop:anchor-sign-preservation-excludes-first-rooting}
and Corollary~\ref{cor:no-crossing-adjacent-two-odd-zero-under-anchor-sign-preservation}
exclude rooted crossing on continuation intervals where the anchor-side value
keeps fixed sign; Proposition~\ref{prop:odd-anchor-passage-no-reset} rules out
rooted crossing at an odd anchor zero itself or immediately after passage; and
Proposition~\ref{prop:universality-threshold-current-route-two-package}
together with
Corollary~\ref{cor:current-route-two-package-universal-under-normalization}
show that even delayed rooted crossing on dangerous post-anchor chambers cannot
be excluded from the current planar/route-2 package alone.

Accordingly, this remark should be read only as local fold data. The remaining
route-2 burden is no longer a ``first-fold exclusion'' theorem, but the search
for the first genuinely non-universal source-coupled input beyond the normalized
planar model $(\mathcal Z,\mathcal R,D_a)$.
\end{remark}
```

```latex
\begin{remark}[Ceiling of the present scalar/discriminant analysis]
\label{rem:ceiling-present-scalar-discriminant-analysis}
The preceding results sharply delimit what can and cannot be obtained from the
current planar/scalar reformulation.

On the positive-kernel side, one-sign-change chambers are sterile for genuine
repeated-source first loss:
the born critical branch is simple, has strictly negative slope, and cannot
satisfy
\[
D_a(\tau(a))=\mathcal Z(a)
\]
before the active segment acquires another odd zero of $\mathcal R$
(Proposition~\ref{prop:first-rooting-requires-second-odd-zero-repeated-source}).
On the discriminant side, the adjacent-odd-zero entrance itself cannot create
the first rooted point
(Proposition~\ref{prop:discriminant-entry-not-first-root}).

The new anchor-sign and odd-anchor-passage arguments remove a substantial part
of the remaining freedom. On any continuation interval on which the anchor-side
value
\[
\mathcal R(a)
\]
keeps fixed sign, the RH-selected slice
\[
\gamma=\mathcal Z(a)
\]
cannot cross the continued discriminant curve. When the anchor itself passes
through an odd-order zero of $\mathcal R$, the integrating-factor defect keeps
its incoming sign across that odd anchor zero, so a rooted crossing cannot occur
there or immediately after it. The ensuing post-anchor chambers then alternate
dangerous and safe, beginning with a dangerous first post-anchor chamber.

However, two no-go facts now show that the present scalar/discriminant package
has reached its ceiling. First,
Remark~\ref{rem:no-go-local-scalar-first-dangerous-chamber} shows that already
on the first dangerous post-anchor chamber, the local normalized rooted
equations and fold/transversality data are formally realizable in the planar
scalar model. Second,
Proposition~\ref{prop:universality-threshold-current-route-two-package} and
Corollary~\ref{cor:current-route-two-package-universal-under-normalization}
show that the entire current route-2 source package
\[
\Psi_a,\qquad
\mathfrak D,\qquad
\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}},\qquad
D_{f_a}
\]
is universal under normalization: every analytic normalized planar model lifts
to a genuine analytic source model for this package.

Accordingly, after the fixed-sign and odd-anchor exclusions, the remaining
problem is \emph{not} a delayed no-crossing / profile-realizability problem
inside the present scalar/discriminant package. It is to find the first
genuinely non-universal source-coupled input, i.e. structure not already
captured by the normalized planar model $(\mathcal Z,\mathcal R,D_a)$.

So any further progress on the nonmixed repeated-source branch must use
genuinely source-coupled structure beyond the present universal package,
possibly through stronger provenance laws, higher canonical/mixed data, or
another RH-specific input invisible in the planar normalized model.
\end{remark}
```

```latex
\begin{remark}[What route 2 now reduces to]
\label{rem:route-two-reduces-to-global-no-crossing}
The discriminant analysis first showed that a rooted point is not born
\emph{at the entry} into the adjacent-two-odd-zero chamber. The stronger
anchor-sign argument showed more: on any continuation interval on which the
anchor-side value
\[
\mathcal R(a)
\]
keeps a fixed sign, the RH-selected slice
\[
\gamma=\mathcal Z(a)
\]
cannot cross the discriminant curve at all.

The odd-anchor analysis sharpened this further: when the anchor itself passes
through an odd-order zero of $\mathcal R$, the integrating-factor defect
\[
\mathscr G(a)=e^{-\mathcal A(a)}\bigl(D_a(\tau(a))-\mathcal Z(a)\bigr)
\]
keeps its incoming sign across that odd anchor zero, so a rooted crossing cannot
occur there or immediately after passage. The subsequent post-anchor chambers
then alternate dangerous and safe, beginning with a dangerous first post-anchor
chamber
(Corollary~\ref{cor:first-post-anchor-chamber-dangerous}).

However, two no-go facts are now clear. First,
Remark~\ref{rem:no-go-local-scalar-first-dangerous-chamber} shows that already
on that first dangerous post-anchor chamber, the local normalized rooted
equations and fold data are formally realizable in the planar scalar model.
Second, the current route-2 source package itself is still universal under the
normalized lift
\[
c=1,\qquad v_5=t,\qquad \lambda=t^2,\qquad u_5''=2\mathcal Z
\]
(Proposition~\ref{prop:universality-threshold-current-route-two-package}),
so even the source-level objects
\[
\Psi_a,\qquad \mathfrak D,\qquad \mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}},\qquad D_{f_a}
\]
do not yet distinguish the RH branch from an arbitrary analytic normalized
model.

So route 2 no longer reduces merely to a delayed no-crossing /
profile-realizability problem \emph{within the current package}. It reduces to
finding the first genuinely \emph{non-universal} source-coupled input, i.e. an
ingredient not already captured by the normalized planar $D_a$ model.

Within the present draft, the first plausible places for such new input lie
beyond the current universal quartet, for example in continuum-strength
provenance constraints on $q$ over whole one-pair blocks, or in external
mixed/canonical structure not already absorbed by the normalized planar model.
\end{remark}
```

```latex
\begin{remark}[What the quotient-transport package does and does not prove]
\label{rem:what-quotient-transport-package-does-and-does-not-prove}
The quotient-transport package gives a sharp \emph{pointwise} reduction of the
residual exact fixed-shear $K_v=0$ slice. In particular,
Proposition~\ref{prop:quotient-transport-scalar-residual-ladder-fixed-shear-Kv-zero}
shows that the pointwise residual geometry is organized by the one-dimensional
quotient transport scalar
\[
\widehat{\mathcal D}(u)=\widehat Q'(u),
\qquad
u=t^2,
\]
and
Corollary~\ref{cor:quartic-sextic-quotient-injectivity-local-no-reentry}
shows that in the quartic--sextic rung the quotient branch is locally
one-sheeted.

What is \emph{not} proved here is any global barrier / critical-value-ordering
theorem for the residual $K_v=0$ lane. In particular, the present draft does
not yet show that the full transported overlap state relevant to the later
finite-core problem is already visible in the quotient branch data, nor that
global no-reentry follows from pointwise quotient compression alone.

Accordingly, the quotient-transport package should be read as a reduction of
the mixed residual problem to a global quotient-visible transport /
no-hidden-reset theorem, not as an already completed closure of the residual
exact fixed-shear lane.
\end{remark}
```

Those five edits capture the real current state: route 2 is exhausted **inside its present universal package**, the remaining nonmixed task is to find a genuinely non-universal source-coupled input, and the quotient-transport side should be described as a **local/pointwise reduction plus a remaining no-hidden-reset problem**, not as a completed global closure. turn22file1turn22file2 

If you want, the next step is for me to do one more pass and give you a very short “delete nothing else / these are final” audit against this exact draft.

## Assistant (2026-04-21 16:23:51)

_Thought for 3m 10s_

Yes. I think there is one more clean theorem we can honestly extract on Attack A, and it sharpens the frontier quite a bit.

The setup already in the notes is:

- the current lower route-2 package is universal under normalization, so nothing phrased only in \((\mathcal Z,\mathcal R,D_a)\), \(\Psi_a\), \(\mathfrak D\), \(\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}\), \(D_{f_a}\) can distinguish the RH branch from an arbitrary normalized planar model; there is even an explicit analytic source-level countermodel realizing the delayed-crossing scenario. turn27file1turn27file2
- arbitrary canonical quotient-septic data \(\Delta_7\) is still locally free once the lower one-pair data are fixed, so “use \(\Delta_7\)” by itself is not yet a genuine source-coupled rigidity theorem. turn30file2
- on a generic one-pair block, the highest-new direct slice is
\[
\phi=A\,q^{(7)},
\]
with \(A\) generically nonvanishing, and this direct slice is itself fully universal on the block; moreover the existing no-go result already says any finite family of **linear** provenance constraints on \(q\) is too weak. turn30file1turn31file2turn31file3

The natural next push is therefore to upgrade “finite linear constraints are too weak” to:

\[
\boxed{\text{any finite jet-level provenance constraint is too weak.}}
\]

That is stronger, and it seems provable.

## Proposed theorem

Let \(J\) be a generic one-pair block on which \(A\neq 0\), and work on the direct slice
\[
\phi=A\,q^{(7)}.
\]

Fix finitely many points \(\xi_1,\dots,\xi_m\in J\), and let \(\mathcal J(q)\) denote the finite jet vector
\[
\mathcal J(q)=\bigl(q^{(r)}(\xi_i)\bigr)_{1\le i\le m,\;0\le r\le R_i}.
\]

Suppose \(\Sigma\subset \mathbb R^N\) is any **compatible finite jet condition** on \(\mathcal J(q)\): for example, finitely many equalities/inequalities/algebraic relations among those jet coordinates, with at least one admissible jet vector.

Then any prescribed finite direct-slice recurrence jet pattern for \(\phi\) at finitely many interior points of \(J\) can be realized simultaneously with \(\mathcal J(q)\in\Sigma\) by a polynomial \(q\).

In particular, no theorem using only the explicit direct formula
\[
\phi=A\,q^{(7)}
\]
together with finitely many pointwise provenance conditions on jets of \(q\) can exclude bitangent, four-secant, or same-slope recurrence geometry on the direct slice.

## Why this looks true

A bitangent / same-slope / four-secant pattern for the graph \(y=\phi(\mu)\) is a **finite jet condition on \(\phi\)** at finitely many points. For example, if \(\ell(\mu)=s\mu+b\) is tangent to \(\phi\) at \(\mu_1,\mu_2\), then
\[
\phi(\mu_j)=\ell(\mu_j),\qquad \phi_\mu(\mu_j)=s\qquad (j=1,2).
\]
But since
\[
\phi=A\,q^{(7)},\qquad \phi_\mu=A' q^{(7)}+A q^{(8)},
\]
these become finite jet conditions on \(q\) at the same points. This is exactly the mechanism already used in the linear no-go corollary. 

Now take the union of:

- the finitely many provenance jet conditions on \(q\),
- the finitely many recurrence jet conditions coming from \(\phi\),
- and, if needed, any finite collection of endpoint matching conditions.

All of that is still only a condition on a **finite jet vector** of \(q\) at finitely many points.

Once you specify a compatible jet vector, standard Hermite interpolation gives a polynomial realizing it. That is the whole point: the map
\[
q \longmapsto \mathcal J(q)
\]
from sufficiently high-degree polynomials to finite jet space is surjective.

So the direct-slice recurrence pattern survives not only finite linear provenance laws, but any finite compatible jet-level provenance law whatsoever.

## Clean proof skeleton

Here is the argument in a compact form.

Take all points that appear in the provenance constraints and in the desired recurrence pattern:
\[
\Xi=\{\xi_1,\dots,\xi_m,\mu_1,\dots,\mu_k\}.
\]
Choose an order \(R\) large enough to contain every derivative order that appears.

Define the total jet map on polynomials of degree \(\le N\):
\[
\mathcal H_N:\mathbb P_N \to \prod_{\zeta\in\Xi}\mathbb R^{R+1},\qquad
q\mapsto \bigl(q^{(r)}(\zeta)\bigr)_{\zeta\in\Xi,\,0\le r\le R}.
\]
For \(N\) large enough, \(\mathcal H_N\) is surjective by Hermite interpolation.

The desired direct-slice recurrence pattern imposes finitely many algebraic conditions on the target jet vector because \(\phi\) and its derivatives are linear combinations of jets of \(q\) with coefficients built from \(A\) and its derivatives. The provenance hypotheses also impose finitely many conditions on the same target jet vector.

If those conditions are compatible, choose a jet vector satisfying all of them. By surjectivity of \(\mathcal H_N\), there is a polynomial \(q\) realizing that jet vector. Then \(q\) satisfies the provenance conditions and produces the prescribed recurrence geometry for \(\phi=Aq^{(7)}\).

That proves the theorem.

## What this buys us

This is stronger than the current “finite linear provenance too weak” statement. It kills a broader class of possible next moves:

- finitely many nonlinear boundary matching identities,
- finitely many pointwise positivity/negativity conditions on jets of \(q\),
- finitely many algebraic relations among selected values of \(q,\dots,q^{(r)}\),
- finitely many local barrier conditions at selected points.

All of those are still finite-codimension jet-space restrictions, and the direct slice remains flexible enough to realize recurrence alongside them.

So the next useful theorem really does have to be **continuum-strength**, just as the notes suggest: a pointwise law on an entire block, a nonlocal integral/transport law, or a genuinely external mixed/canonical coupling that acts over a continuum of points rather than finitely many jets. turn31file2turn31file4

## The sharpened frontier

So after this push, Attack A looks like:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Finite-codimension provenance is dead; only continuum-strength provenance can still matter.}
}
\]

That means the next live subproblem is no longer about \(\phi\)-geometry itself. It is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{derive a blockwise law for } q \text{ from genuinely mixed/canonical provenance.}
}
\]

The best concrete target is a relation of one of these types on a generic one-pair block \(J\):

\[
F\bigl(h,q(h),q'(h),\dots,q^{(r)}(h);\text{other canonical data at }h\bigr)=0
\quad\text{for all }h\in J,
\]
or a sign law
\[
F(\cdots)\ge 0 \quad\text{for all }h\in J,
\]
or a nonlocal law
\[
\int_J K(h,\xi)\,q(\xi)\,d\xi = \text{controlled quantity}.
\]

That is the first kind of input not already killed by universality of the lower route-2 package, local freedom of arbitrary \(\Delta_7\), and universality of the direct slice \(\phi=Aq^{(7)}\). turn28file0turn30file1turn31file2

If you want, I’ll turn this into draft-ready LaTeX as a proposition plus a short “what this leaves open” remark.

I’m pushing past the “finite jets are too weak” point now. The goal is to see whether we can turn that ceiling into a sharper theorem, or whether the next viable move has to be a genuinely continuum-strength provenance law.

_Thought for 2m 36s_

Yes. I think there is one more honest push here.

The safe strengthening is not “some arbitrary nonlinear functional package is too weak” in full generality. That would need extra compatibility work. But we **can** strengthen the current no-go from “finite linear provenance constraints are too weak” to:

\[
\boxed{\text{any provenance condition depending only on finitely many pointwise jets of }q\text{ is too weak.}}
\]

That is a real advance beyond the present draft state. Right now the notes already support three facts: the direct highest-new slice is
\[
\phi=A\,q^{(7)},
\]
it is fully universal on a generic one-pair block, and even finite families of linear provenance / matching conditions do not stop bitangent or related recurrence geometry. The notes then identify the next live target as a genuinely continuum-strength law for \(q\) on a whole block.   

Here is the stronger theorem I think we can now safely add to the mathematical picture.

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Finite jet provenance is too weak on the direct slice.}
}
\]

Let \(J\) be a generic one-pair block on which \(A\neq 0\). Fix finitely many points
\[
\xi_1,\dots,\xi_m\in J
\]
and nonnegative integers \(R_1,\dots,R_m\). Prescribe any compatible jet data
\[
q^{(r)}(\xi_i)=a_{i,r},
\qquad
1\le i\le m,\quad 0\le r\le R_i.
\]
Also fix a finite direct-slice recurrence pattern for \(\phi=Aq^{(7)}\) at finitely many interior points. For example, for a bitangent to a chosen affine line \(\ell(\mu)=s\mu+b\) at two points \(\mu_1\neq\mu_2\), prescribe
\[
\phi(\mu_j)=\ell(\mu_j),
\qquad
\phi_\mu(\mu_j)=s
\qquad (j=1,2).
\]

Then there exists a polynomial \(q\) on \(J\) realizing **both** the prescribed provenance jets and the prescribed direct-slice recurrence pattern.

The proof is straightforward. Any finite recurrence pattern for \(\phi\) at finitely many points becomes a finite jet condition on \(q\), because
\[
\phi=Aq^{(7)},\qquad
\phi_\mu=A' q^{(7)}+A q^{(8)},
\]
and higher \(\mu\)-derivatives of \(\phi\) are linear combinations of jets of \(q\) of orders \(7,8,\dots\). So after collecting all provenance points and all recurrence points, the problem becomes one finite Hermite interpolation problem for \(q\). Since polynomial jets at finitely many points are freely prescribable, any compatible combined jet data are realizable by a polynomial. So the direct-slice recurrence event survives arbitrary finite pointwise provenance constraints on \(q\). This strictly strengthens the current “finite linear provenance is too weak” corollary. 

That gives a sharper no-go corollary:

\[
\boxed{
\text{No theorem using only } \phi=Aq^{(7)} \text{ plus finitely many pointwise jet conditions on } q
\text{ can exclude direct-slice recurrence.}
}
\]

This kills a broader class of candidate attacks than the current draft wording does. It rules out not only finitely many linear jet constraints, but also arbitrary nonlinear algebraic conditions on finitely many values
\[
q(\xi_i),q'(\xi_i),\dots,q^{(R_i)}(\xi_i),
\]
because once those jets are fixed, the recurrence conditions are just more jet conditions at more points.

So the frontier sharpens to this:

- finite jet provenance is dead;
- arbitrary canonical \(\Delta_7\) is too free;
- the explicit direct slice \(Aq^{(7)}\) is still universal on a block;
- therefore the next live theorem really does have to be **continuum-strength** on \(q\), not another finite-jet or finite-boundary refinement.   

That means the next serious sub-attacks are now very narrow:

First, try to derive a **blockwise differential law** for \(q\):
\[
L\bigl(h,q,q',\dots,q^{(r)}\bigr)=\text{known lower-order source data}
\quad\text{on }J,
\]
with \(r<7\) or at least not equivalent to freely prescribing \(q^{(7)}\).

Second, try for a **sign-definite integral law** on \(q\) over a whole block:
\[
\int_J K(h,\xi)\,q(\xi)\,d\xi=\text{controlled quantity},
\]
or an inequality version.

Third, try for an **external mixed/canonical coupling** that constrains \(q\) on an interval, not at finitely many points.

So the attack result is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the first possibly useful provenance law must constrain } q \text{ on a continuum, not just finitely many jets.}
}
\]

The cleanest next thing is for me to write this as a draft-ready proposition and corollary.

## Assistant (2026-04-21 16:35:35)

I’m now trying to move from the ceiling statement to the next actual theorem: either a stronger no-go that kills all finite-order attacks at once, or a concrete continuum-strength candidate law for \(q\) that the current notes are already hinting at.

_Thought for 1m 30s_

Yes. There is one more real push here, and I think it is the right one.

The key observation is that the notes already give something **stronger than finite-jet flexibility**: on a generic one-pair block, the direct highest-new slice
\[
\phi=A\,q^{(7)}
\]
is not merely jet-surjective, it is **fully blockwise universal**. For any analytic \(\psi\) on the block, one can construct \(q\) with
\[
\phi=\psi.
\]
And the same notes make the induced \(7\)-state transport explicit:
\[
Q(h):=(q,q',\dots,q^{(6)})(h),\qquad
Q(b)=T_{b-a}Q(a)+\int_a^b K(b-s)\,\frac{\phi(s)}{A(s)}\,ds.
\]
So the whole semiglobal behavior of the direct slice is just forcing in a free seventh-order transport system. turn35file3

That lets us strengthen the no-go one step beyond “finite jet provenance is too weak.” The stronger statement is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{any finite-dimensional affine block-transport constraint is still too weak.}
}
\]

What I mean by that is: suppose on one generic block you impose any finite collection of conditions of the following kinds:

- finitely many endpoint/state conditions on
  \[
  Q(a),\ Q(b),\ Q(c),\dots
  \]
- finitely many linear block moments such as
  \[
  \int_J w_j(h)\,\phi(h)\,dh=c_j
  \quad\text{or}\quad
  \int_J \widetilde w_j(h)\,q(h)\,dh=\widetilde c_j,
  \]
- plus a prescribed direct-slice recurrence template for \(\phi\), such as a chosen bitangent pattern with fixed tangency points and slope.

Then, provided the resulting finite system is compatible, it is still realizable by choosing \(\phi\) first and then reconstructing \(q\) from the integral formula above. The reason is that all those endpoint/state/moment constraints are just **finite linear functionals of the forcing \(\phi\)**, while a prescribed recurrence template for \(\phi\) is again only a finite set of jet conditions on \(\phi\). Since \(\phi\) itself is arbitrary analytic on the whole block, there is still enormous room left after imposing finitely many such conditions. turn35file4

So the honest strengthened frontier is this:

\[
\boxed{
\text{not just finite pointwise provenance, but even finite-dimensional semiglobal provenance, is dead on the direct slice.}
}
\]

This is stronger than the current draft’s “finite linear provenance/matching conditions on \(q\) are too weak.” The state-transport formula shows that even if someone tries to rescue the lane by adding finitely many endpoint or blockwise linear transport conditions, they are still only finite-dimensional affine restrictions on an otherwise arbitrary analytic forcing \(\phi\). That is not enough to kill bitangent / four-secant / same-slope recurrence templates on the direct graph. turn35file4

That, in turn, tells us the next theorem has to look like one of only three types.

First, a **continuum-strength differential law** for \(q\) on a whole block, for example
\[
L\bigl(h,q,q',\dots,q^{(r)}\bigr)=\text{known lower-order source data},
\]
with \(r<7\), or at least not equivalent to arbitrary prescription of \(q^{(7)}\). Such a law would collapse the forcing freedom and make \(\phi=Aq^{(7)}\) non-arbitrary. The notes already point to this as the most natural next move. turn35file2

Second, a **continuum-strength integral law** for \(q\) or \(\phi\), not finitely many moments but a genuine family in \(h\), something like a Volterra/Fredholm relation
\[
\phi(h)=F(h)+\int_J L(h,\xi)\,q(\xi)\,d\xi
\]
or a sign-definite kernel inequality holding for every \(h\in J\). That would cut the analytic forcing class down to infinite codimension, which is exactly what the present no-go results say is necessary. turn35file2

Third, a genuinely **external mixed/canonical coupling** that constrains \(q\) across the whole block and is not already absorbed by the normalized planar model. The notes are explicit that arbitrary quotient-septic \(\Delta_7\) is still too free, so the target cannot be “some new \(\Delta_7\) statement”; it has to be a provenance-sensitive law that survives blockwise, not just at finitely many points. turn35file2

So the cleanest current attack result is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The direct-slice lane is exhausted against all finite-dimensional attacks.}
}
\]

What remains is not another jet theorem, not another endpoint matching theorem, and not another finite-moment theorem. The first live theorem now has to be an **infinite-codimension blockwise law** for \(q\) or \(\phi\).

The most promising next sub-attack inside Attack A is this:

\[
\boxed{
\text{derive a Volterra-type block law for }q\text{ from the mixed/canonical package.}
}
\]

That is, try to isolate some source or canonical identity that, once restricted to a generic one-pair block, becomes a relation of the form
\[
q^{(7)}(h)=G\!\left(h;\ q|_{(-\infty,h]};\ \text{lower-order canonical data}\right),
\]
or equivalently
\[
\phi(h)=A(h)\,G(\cdots),
\]
for every \(h\) in the block. If you get anything of that type, even weakly, the full-block universality of \(\phi\) is gone and the direct-slice geometric dictionary becomes live again. turn35file1turn35file2

So my honest status report is: I do think Attack A has now been pushed one notch further. The new ceiling is not just “finite jets are too weak,” but “finite-dimensional semiglobal block transport is too weak.” The next theorem has to be genuinely continuum-strength.
## User (2026-04-21 16:38:19)

## Assistant (2026-04-21 16:38:22)

I’m drilling into the exact direct-slice and universality statements in the attached draft now, to see whether there’s a real next theorem hiding there or whether the only honest move is to isolate the precise form a continuum-strength law would have to take.

_Thought for 1m 30s_

Yes. I think the strongest further push I can justify is a **gauge-rigidity theorem** for the direct provenance variable \(q\).

The current draft/notes already say three things very clearly: on a generic one-pair block the direct slice is
\[
\phi=A\,q^{(7)},
\]
this slice is fully universal blockwise, and even finite linear provenance/matching conditions on \(q\) do not kill direct-slice recurrence. They also say the next live target must therefore be either a continuum-strength provenance law for \(q\) or a genuinely external mixed/canonical input. turn37file3turn38file1turn38file4

The right new theorem is this.

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Any pointwise order-}\le 6\textbf{ law that respects the }\Pi_6\textbf{-gauge is vacuous in }q.
}
\]

Here \(\Pi_6\) means the polynomials of degree at most \(6\). The reason this is the natural gauge is that the direct slice only sees \(q\) through \(q^{(7)}\), so
\[
q\longmapsto q+P,\qquad P\in \Pi_6,
\]
leaves \(\phi=Aq^{(7)}\) unchanged.

Now let \(J\) be a generic one-pair block, let \(B_1,\dots,B_m\) be any analytic external scalar fields on \(J\), and suppose we have a pointwise relation
\[
F\bigl(h,B_1(h),\dots,B_m(h),q(h),q'(h),\dots,q^{(r)}(h)\bigr)=0
\qquad (h\in J),
\]
with \(r\le 6\), which is invariant under
\[
q\mapsto q+P,\qquad P\in \Pi_6.
\]

Then this law is actually independent of \(q\). Equivalently, it reduces to
\[
F\bigl(h,B_1(h),\dots,B_m(h)\bigr)=0.
\]

The proof is short and clean. Fix a point \(h_0\in J\). The map
\[
P\in \Pi_6\longmapsto \bigl(P(h_0),P'(h_0),\dots,P^{(6)}(h_0)\bigr)\in \mathbf C^7
\]
is surjective: given any target jet \((a_0,\dots,a_6)\), the Taylor polynomial
\[
P(h)=\sum_{j=0}^6 \frac{a_j}{j!}(h-h_0)^j
\]
has exactly those derivatives at \(h_0\). So by adding a suitable \(P\in\Pi_6\), we can change the jet
\[
\bigl(q(h_0),q'(h_0),\dots,q^{(r)}(h_0)\bigr)
\]
to any other jet of order \(r\le 6\), while keeping \(\phi=Aq^{(7)}\) fixed. If \(F\) is invariant under all such gauge shifts, then at fixed external data \(B_j(h_0)\) it must take the same value on every \(r\)-jet of \(q\). So it cannot actually depend on those \(q\)-jets at all.

That is a genuine strengthening of the current ceiling. It says not only that finite linear provenance is too weak, but that **every intrinsic pointwise law of order at most \(6\)** is automatically powerless, provided it respects the natural \(\Pi_6\)-ambiguity of the direct slice. In other words, lower-order pointwise dependence on \(q\) cannot be the missing rigidity.

There is also an order-\(7\) version.

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Any pointwise order-}\le 7\textbf{ gauge-invariant law reduces to a law in }q^{(7)}\textbf{ alone.}
}
\]

More precisely, if
\[
F\bigl(h,B(h),q(h),q'(h),\dots,q^{(7)}(h)\bigr)=0
\]
is invariant under \(q\mapsto q+P\) for all \(P\in\Pi_6\), then the same transitivity argument kills dependence on \(q,\dots,q^{(6)}\), so the law must factor as
\[
G\bigl(h,B(h),q^{(7)}(h)\bigr)=0.
\]
Since
\[
q^{(7)}=\frac{\phi}{A},
\]
this is equivalently
\[
\widetilde G\bigl(h,B(h),\phi(h)\bigr)=0.
\]

That is the sharp pointwise frontier. Any useful **pointwise** continuation must do one of two things:

either it introduces genuinely external fields \(B\) not already absorbed by the current universal package, and couples them directly to \(q^{(7)}\) or \(\phi\);

or it breaks out of the pointwise framework entirely and gives a nonlocal / continuum-strength law on the whole block.

So the attack result is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{order-}\le 6\text{ pointwise intrinsic laws are dead; the first live pointwise law must touch }q^{(7)}\text{ itself via external data.}
}
\]

I want to be careful about one limitation. This does **not** prove that no order-\(\le 6\) law exists anywhere in the full RH provenance package. It proves something slightly more precise: if a proposed law is genuinely intrinsic to the direct provenance representation and respects the natural \(q\sim q+\Pi_6\) ambiguity, then lower-order pointwise \(q\)-dependence cannot matter. So the next honest pointwise target is a law of the form
\[
H\bigl(h,\text{external mixed/canonical fields},\,q^{(7)}(h)\bigr)=0
\]
or a sign law of the same type. And if nothing like that exists, then only a nonlocal block law remains. That lines up exactly with the notes’ conclusion that the next live target must be either nonlocal, or pointwise but genuinely external. turn38file4

The next attack I would make is to identify candidate external fields and ask a very blunt question about each one:

does it survive the universality lift, or does it truly constrain \(q^{(7)}\) pointwise in a way the planar model cannot fake?

If you want, I’ll now push that exact question against the concrete candidates already floating in the draft, like \([A_7^{\mathfrak f}]\), \(\Delta_7\), and the mixed/canonical order-7 fields.

_Thought for 58s_

I pushed Attack A one step further, and the strongest honest conclusion is another **no-go**, but a useful one.

The draft/notes now support this much:

After the lower one-pair data \((c,u_5,v_5)\) are fixed, the canonical septic residual
\[
\Delta_7=u_7v_5-u_5v_7
\]
is still locally free. On \(v_5\neq 0\) one can gauge-fix \(v_7^{\mathrm{new}}=0\), \(u_7^{\mathrm{new}}=\Delta_7/v_5\), and similarly on \(u_5\neq 0\) one can gauge-fix \(u_7^{\mathrm{new}}=0\), \(v_7^{\mathrm{new}}=-\Delta_7/u_5\). So arbitrary quotient-septic geometry of \((c,v_5,\Delta_7)\) is still formally realizable once the lower data are fixed. turn41file1

That kills the naive hybrid
\[
\text{route 2} + \Delta_7
\]
as a closure strategy. In particular, tangent/separator claims, secant/incidence claims, ECT/convexity claims for the quotient-septic curve, and local sign restrictions phrased only in terms of arbitrary \(\Delta_7\) remain formally realizable. The notes say this explicitly: the lower quartet plus arbitrary quotient-septic geometry is still universal, so \(\Delta_7\) by itself is not yet the first genuinely non-universal ingredient. turn41file3

The next layer down is no better. The same notes record that the direct highest-new provenance slice
\[
\phi=A\,q^{(7)}
\]
is fully universal on each generic one-pair block, and even any finite family of linear provenance conditions on \(q\) is too weak to exclude direct-slice recurrence. They then sharpen that frontier to: the next viable target must be a continuum-strength provenance law for \(q\), or an external mixed/canonical theorem that constrains \(q\) on a whole block. turn41file2turn41file4

The clean extra inference from that setup is this.

Because the direct slice only sees \(q\) through \(q^{(7)}\), it is invariant under the gauge
\[
q \mapsto q+P,\qquad P\in \Pi_6.
\]
So any **pointwise** law on a block that depends only on \(q,\dots,q^{(6)}\) and is supposed to be intrinsic to the direct provenance representation is automatically suspect: by varying \(P\), you can change the lower jet arbitrarily at a point without changing \(\phi\). That means any useful pointwise law must either touch \(q^{(7)}\) itself, or import genuinely external fields not already absorbed by the universal model. This part is an inference from the direct-slice formula, not something the notes state verbatim. It fits the draft frontier very well, but I would still treat it as a new argument rather than something already proved in the paper. Its premise is the direct-slice formula and universality above. 

So the attack result is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{canonical order-7 closure alone is still too free;}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{the first live theorem must be provenance-sensitive at order 7, or continuum-strength in }q.
}
\]

That narrows the next attack a lot. I would now aim at one of exactly two theorem shapes.

The first is a **canonical septic-coupling lemma**: prove that on the actual RH branch, the canonical order-7 data are not free, but satisfy a relation tying \(\Delta_7\) to \([A_7^{\mathfrak f}]\) or to mixed data, in a way the free quotient-septic model cannot imitate. This is exactly the frontier the notes identify after killing naive “route 2 + \(\Delta_7\)” geometry. 

The second is a **continuum-strength provenance law for \(q\)** on a generic one-pair block:
\[
F\bigl(h,q(h),q'(h),\dots,q^{(r)}(h);\text{external canonical data at }h\bigr)=0
\quad\text{for all }h\in J,
\]
or a nonlocal version. The notes are explicit that finite pointwise/finite-codimension constraints are dead, so only a whole-interval law is still live. 

So my honest answer is: Attack A has now reached a sharper ceiling. I do **not** see a proof from arbitrary \([A_7^{\mathfrak f}]\) or arbitrary \(\Delta_7\) geometry alone. The real next move is to look for a law that says the **actual RH** \(\Delta_7\) is not arbitrary once one follows the moving shear \(f_a=u_5-\mathcal Z(a)\lambda\), or else to derive a whole-block law for \(q\).

The best concrete next push is to attack this statement:

\[
\boxed{
\text{On the actual RH branch, the moving-shear canonical septic residual is not a free }y-mx\text{ family.}
}
\]

In practice that means: derive the canonical order-7 residual attached to
\[
f_a=u_5-\mathcal Z(a)\lambda
\]
inside the order-7 closure language, and see whether its dependence on \(a\) forces a relation with \([A_7^{\mathfrak f}]\) or mixed data that a delayed rooted crossing would violate. That is the first attack not already killed by the universality/no-go results above.

## Assistant (2026-04-21 16:43:50)

I’m now digging for the concrete order-7 objects around the moving shear \(f_a=u_5-\mathcal Z(a)\lambda\), because that’s the first place a genuinely non-free canonical relation might still survive the universality no-gos.

I found a sharper reduction: after quotienting out the natural \(q\mapsto q+\Pi_6\) gauge, any surviving pointwise theorem is no longer really a theorem about \(q\) at all — it becomes a local differential law for the direct slice \(\phi=A\,q^{(7)}\). That narrows the search a lot.

_Thought for 46s_

Here is the strongest clean continuation I can justify.

I think the right next theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{every gauge-invariant pointwise law for }q\text{ reduces to a local differential law for }\phi=A\,q^{(7)}.
}
\]

That is useful because it converts the search for a provenance law on \(q\) into a much more concrete search for a law on the direct highest-new scalar \(\phi\).

The notes already support the input you need for this: on a generic one-pair block the direct highest-new slice is
\[
\phi=A\,q^{(7)},
\]
with \(A\) generically nonvanishing, and this direct slice is the first provenance-sensitive scalar that survives all the earlier no-go reductions. turn43file1

Now take a generic one-pair block \(J\), and let
\[
B_1(h),\dots,B_m(h)
\]
denote arbitrary external mixed/canonical coefficient fields. Consider a pointwise law of finite order \(r\):
\[
F\bigl(h,B(h),q(h),q'(h),\dots,q^{(r)}(h)\bigr)=0
\qquad (h\in J),
\]
and assume it is intrinsic to the direct provenance representation, meaning it is invariant under the natural gauge
\[
q\mapsto q+P,\qquad P\in \Pi_6,
\]
because this gauge leaves \(q^{(7)}\), hence \(\phi\), unchanged.

We already pushed one part of this: if \(r\le 6\), gauge invariance kills the \(q\)-dependence entirely, so the law reduces to a relation among the external fields alone. That means no order-\(\le 6\) pointwise law can constrain the direct slice. 

The new step is what happens for \(r\ge 7\).

Since
\[
q^{(7)}=\frac{\phi}{A},
\]
differentiating gives
\[
q^{(8)}
=
\left(\frac{\phi}{A}\right)'
=
\frac{1}{A}\phi'
-\frac{A'}{A^2}\phi,
\]
and then
\[
q^{(9)}
=
\left(\frac{1}{A}\phi'
-\frac{A'}{A^2}\phi\right)'
=
\frac{1}{A}\phi''
+\text{lower-order terms in }\phi,\phi'.
\]
Inductively, for each \(j\ge 0\),
\[
q^{(7+j)}
=
L_j(h,\partial_h)\phi,
\]
where \(L_j\) is a scalar linear differential operator of order \(j\) with analytic coefficients built from \(A\) and its derivatives. The leading term is always
\[
\frac{1}{A}\phi^{(j)}.
\]

So once gauge invariance has removed dependence on \(q,\dots,q^{(6)}\), any pointwise law of order \(r\) must factor as
\[
\widetilde F\bigl(h,B(h),q^{(7)}(h),q^{(8)}(h),\dots,q^{(r)}(h)\bigr)=0,
\]
and therefore becomes
\[
\widehat F\bigl(h,B(h),\phi(h),\phi'(h),\dots,\phi^{(r-7)}(h)\bigr)=0.
\]

That is the real reduction theorem.

So the attack result is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the first viable pointwise theorem is not a theorem on }q\text{ per se; it is a local ODE-type law for }\phi.
}
\]

This sharpens the frontier considerably.

If there were a useful order-\(7\) pointwise external law, it would have to look like
\[
G\bigl(h,B(h),\phi(h)\bigr)=0,
\]
so \(\phi\) would be pointwise determined algebraically by external mixed/canonical fields. That would kill the direct-slice universality immediately.

If there were a useful order-\(8\) pointwise external law, it would become a first-order differential law
\[
G\bigl(h,B(h),\phi(h),\phi'(h)\bigr)=0.
\]

In general, order \(r\) becomes a local differential law of order \(r-7\) for \(\phi\).

That means the next live pointwise search can now be phrased very concretely:

- either derive an **algebraic law**
  \[
  G(h,B,\phi)=0,
  \]
- or derive a **local differential law**
  \[
  G(h,B,\phi,\phi',\dots,\phi^{(k)})=0,
  \]
with \(B\) genuinely external and non-universal.

This is better than talking vaguely about “a provenance law on \(q\),” because it tells us exactly what form that law must take after gauge reduction.

There is a second useful consequence.

Because the direct-slice lane is already known to be universal as an arbitrary analytic graph unless some extra provenance law intervenes, the only honest pointwise closure route left is to show that the actual RH \(\phi\) belongs to a proper differential class that generic analytic graphs do not belong to. The notes already indicate that abstract graph geometry is spent and only the explicit provenance-sensitive formula for \(\phi\) can still matter. turn43file3

So the clean next attack target is now:

\[
\boxed{
\text{derive a non-universal external differential law for }\phi.
}
\]

More specifically, I would now attack one of these two statements.

First target:
\[
G\bigl(h,\text{mixed/canonical fields},\phi(h)\bigr)=0.
\]
That would be the dream case: a pointwise order-\(7\) algebraic determination of \(\phi\).

Second target:
\[
G\bigl(h,\text{mixed/canonical fields},\phi(h),\phi'(h)\bigr)=0
\]
or a slightly higher-order version. That would still kill full universality of the direct slice and re-open the graph-geometry lane.

So my honest continuation is: we have now reduced the pointwise search all the way to a search for a **differential law for \(\phi\)**, not for \(q\). That is the strongest clean theorem I can justify from the current notes.

The next thing I would attack is whether any of the concrete external order-7 candidates already in the draft — especially \([A_7^{\mathfrak f}]\), \(\Delta_7\), or the moving-shear canonical septic residual — can be rewritten to give an actual algebraic or first-order differential law for \(\phi\), rather than just another free geometric decoration.

_Thought for 1m 28s_

I think the next honest push is now very sharp.

The draft already says the whole current route-2 package is exhausted and universal under normalization, so any further progress has to use a genuinely non-universal source-coupled ingredient; the first candidates named there are exactly the quotient-septic / mixed invariants \([A_7^{\mathfrak f}]\) and \(\Delta_7\). turn45file2

But the same notes also say something important on the higher side: **arbitrary** canonical quotient-septic geometry is still locally free. After the lower one-pair data \((c,u_5,v_5)\) are fixed, \(\Delta_7\) can still be chosen arbitrarily locally, so no theorem that uses only generic quotient-septic geometry of \((c,v_5,\Delta_7)\) can close the branch by itself. And on the direct highest-new slice, the order-7 scalar is already reduced to an ordinary scalar graph
\[
y=\phi(\mu),
\qquad
\phi=A\,q^{(7)},
\]
but that graph is still fully universal blockwise, so by itself it is just a dictionary, not yet a rigidity theorem. turn46file4

So the attack has narrowed to one very specific target:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the moving-shear order-7 data must satisfy a provenance-sensitive law, not merely arbitrary quotient-septic geometry.}
}
\]

That is the right next theorem to attack.

What I can push further right now is the following reduction.

Because the direct highest-new slice only sees \(q\) through \(q^{(7)}\), any pointwise formulation that is intrinsic to that direct slice is insensitive to the gauge
\[
q \mapsto q+P,\qquad P\in \Pi_6.
\]
So if you try to get a pointwise theorem from higher data, then after quotienting out this gauge, it cannot really be a theorem about the lower jets of \(q\). It must reduce to a local law for the direct slice \(\phi=Aq^{(7)}\). This is not quoted verbatim in the notes; it is the clean inference from the direct-slice formula \(\phi=Aq^{(7)}\) together with the universality ceiling already recorded there. 

That gives the first concrete reduction:

\[
\boxed{
\text{If a useful higher-order pointwise law exists, it must become an algebraic or differential law for }\phi.
}
\]

So the first thing I would test is not “does \(\Delta_7\) help in the abstract?” It is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Does the moving-shear family }f_a=u_5-\mathcal Z(a)\lambda
\text{ induce a nontrivial law for its order-7 direct slice }\phi_a?
}
\]

That is where the attack becomes concrete.

The reason this is the right place to push is that the draft’s current frontier is explicitly about hybridizing the repeated-source moving shear
\[
f_a=u_5-\mathcal Z(a)\lambda
\]
with the first non-universal higher data. So the higher object has to be attached to the **moving shear along the continued branch**, not to \(u_5\) or \(\lambda\) separately. turn45file4

The first theorem I would try to prove is therefore this.

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Source-pinned septic obstruction theorem, first reduction form.}
}
\]

Along the continued repeated-source branch \(h=h(a)\) with \(D(a,h(a))=0\), let \(\phi_a\) denote the highest-new direct scalar attached to the moving shear \(f_a=u_5-\mathcal Z(a)\lambda\). Then either:

1. \(\phi_a\) is still completely free as \(a\) varies, in which case the pointwise order-7 route is dead too; or

2. \(\phi_a\) satisfies a local algebraic/ODE-type law
   \[
   G\bigl(a,h,\phi_a,\partial_h\phi_a,\dots\bigr)=0
   \]
   involving genuinely external mixed/canonical coefficients, and that law is the first non-universal input.

That is not proved yet, but it is now the correct theorem shape.

There is one more useful sharpening.

Because the moving shear is affine in the anchor parameter,
\[
f_a=u_5-\mathcal Z(a)\lambda,
\]
the first thing to test is whether the associated highest-new direct scalar is also affine in \(\mathcal Z(a)\), schematically
\[
\phi_a=\phi^{(u_5)}-\mathcal Z(a)\,\phi^{(\lambda)}.
\]
I am writing this schematically because I have not yet verified the exact order-7 normalization/gauge conventions in the draft for the moving-shear slot, so I would not put this in the paper yet. But as an attack, this is the right computation.

If that affine-in-\(\mathcal Z(a)\) split is true, then the whole higher-order route collapses to a two-generator problem:

- two fixed blockwise direct slices, say \(\phi^{(u_5)}\) and \(\phi^{(\lambda)}\),
- sampled along the moving parameter \(\gamma=\mathcal Z(a)\).

Then the question is no longer “some mysterious order-7 invariant.” It becomes:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Can the pencil }\phi^{(u_5)}-\gamma\,\phi^{(\lambda)}
\text{ realize the delayed rooted crossing geometry when }\gamma=\mathcal Z(a)?
}
\]

That is a much better target.

Why? Because once you are in a pencil, there are several real things to test:

- whether the pair \((\phi^{(u_5)},\phi^{(\lambda)})\) has a Wronskian or Chebyshev-type property;
- whether \(\gamma=\mathcal Z(a)\) traverses the dangerous values monotonically along the branch;
- whether the first rooted point plus stationarity of the target map forces a tangency or bitangent event in that pencil which the pair cannot realize.

That would finally be a provenance-sensitive theorem, not arbitrary quotient-septic geometry.

So my current attack conclusion is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the next live computation is to derive the order-7 direct slice for the moving shear }f_a,
\text{ and test whether it forms an affine pencil in }\mathcal Z(a).
}
\]

If it does, that is the first real non-universal foothold I see.

If it does **not**, then the order-7 pointwise route is probably dead too, and what remains is a genuinely nonlocal whole-block law for \(q\) or \(\phi\). That would fit the other ceiling already recorded in the notes, namely that finite-dimensional and purely local direct-slice constraints are too weak. turn46file4

So the next concrete sub-attacks are:

First, compute the exact moving-shear order-7 direct scalar \(\phi_a\).

Second, check whether it splits affinely in \(\mathcal Z(a)\).

Third, if it does, study the two-generator pencil
\[
\phi^{(u_5)}-\gamma\,\phi^{(\lambda)}.
\]

That is where I would keep pushing.

  \]
  and this slice is fully universal blockwise: \(\phi\) can be any analytic scalar graph on the block. turn48file4

So the only honest continuation is to look for a law that is both:

2. strong enough to destroy the full-block universality of \(\phi=Aq^{(7)}\). turn48file4

From there, I think the strongest clean reduction is this:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Any surviving pointwise theorem must reduce to a local differential law for }\phi.
}
\]

That part is new reasoning, but it follows very naturally from the direct-slice formula in the notes. Since
\[
\phi=A\,q^{(7)},
\]
the direct slice is invariant under
\[
q\mapsto q+P,\qquad P\in \Pi_6,
\]
because this does not change \(q^{(7)}\). So any pointwise law that is intrinsic to the direct provenance representation cannot meaningfully depend on \(q,\dots,q^{(6)}\); otherwise it would change under the natural gauge while \(\phi\) stayed fixed. Once you quotient out that gauge, the first meaningful pointwise dependence is on \(q^{(7)}\), hence on \(\phi/A\), and higher derivatives \(q^{(8)},q^{(9)},\dots\) become differential expressions in \(\phi\) with coefficients built from \(A\). So any viable pointwise theorem has to become something like
\[
G\bigl(h,\text{external higher data},\phi,\phi',\dots,\phi^{(k)}\bigr)=0.
\]

That is the first real sharpening beyond the current notes: the search is no longer for “some law on \(q\),” but for a **local ODE-type law for \(\phi\)**.

\[
f_a=u_5-\mathcal Z(a)\lambda
\]
with higher non-universal data, such as \([A_7^{\mathfrak f}]\) or \(\Delta_7\). turn48file3

So the right concrete question is not:

“Does arbitrary \(\Delta_7\) help?”

That is already dead. The right question is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{What is the order-7 direct scalar attached to the moving shear }f_a=u_5-\mathcal Z(a)\lambda\text{?}
}
\]

And more specifically:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Does that moving-shear direct scalar form an affine pencil in }\gamma=\mathcal Z(a)\text{?}
}

\[
\phi_a=\phi^{(u_5)}-\gamma\,\phi^{(\lambda)},
\qquad \gamma=\mathcal Z(a),

or the corresponding version in the exact order-7 closure notation. I have **not** verified the exact formula in the draft yet, so I would not state this as proved. But as an attack, it is the right computation.

\]
sampled along the moving parameter \(\gamma=\mathcal Z(a)\).

- prove its Wronskian cannot change sign in the pattern needed for delayed rooted crossing;
- or show that a first rooted point plus the already-known stationarity/fold data would force a forbidden bitangent or same-slope re-entry inside that pencil.

That would finally be provenance-sensitive in a way the fully universal single-graph model is not.

a two-generator no-recurrence theorem for that pencil.

If the answer is no, then I think the pointwise order-7 route is probably dead too, and what remains is exactly what the notes already suggest: a genuinely continuum-strength, whole-block provenance law for \(q\) or \(\phi\). 

So the next sub-attack I would do is very concrete:

1. write the exact order-7 direct scalar attached to a general sheared object \(y-mx\) in the draft’s closure language;

3. check whether the dependence on \(\mathcal Z(a)\) is affine;

That is the best live attack angle I see now.

I’m checking the exact order-7 closure formulas and the moving-shear notation in the attached draft now, so I can see whether the affine-pencil idea is actually supported by the paper’s own algebra or whether it collapses.

_Thought for 46s_

I pushed it further, and I think the clean next result is this:

\[
\boxed{
\text{At the current package level, any gauge-invariant \emph{linear} local law for }q
\text{ factors through }q^{(7)},\text{ hence through }\phi/A.
}
\]

That is the strongest honest continuation I can justify from the attached thread.

The reason is already implicit in the direct-slice package. On a generic one-pair block,
\[
\phi=A\,q^{(7)},\qquad A\neq 0,
\]
and the draft/notes explicitly treat this slice as fully universal on the block. They also emphasize that even after finitely many linear provenance or matching conditions on \(q\), direct-slice recurrence is still realizable. So the present package only sees \(q\) modulo the natural polynomial gauge
\[
q\sim q+P,\qquad P\in \Pi_6.
\]
That is exactly the frontier the notes record. turn52file1turn52file2turn52file3

Now the quotient view is exact: on an interval,
\[
\mathcal O(J)/\Pi_6 \cong \mathcal O(J),
\qquad
[q]\longmapsto q^{(7)}.
\]
So if a candidate linear provenance operator \(L\) is genuinely canonical for the current package, it must be well-defined on the quotient class \([q]\), hence it must factor through \(q^{(7)}\). Equivalently,
\[
L(q)=\widetilde L\bigl(q^{(7)}\bigr)
=\widetilde L\!\left(\frac{\phi}{A}\right).
\]
That means any such law is not a new theorem about \(q\) at all. It is only a reformulation of the already-visible direct slice. This is exactly the direction the notes themselves are heading when they say that without killing the \(\Pi_6\)-gauge, there is no meaningful local operator theorem left for \(q\), and that any linear operator law must kill the full \(\Pi_6\) gauge. 

So the attack result is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{No new local \emph{linear} provenance theorem exists at the current gauge level, unless it adds data that fix the }7\text{-dimensional gauge.}
}
\]

That sharpens the ceiling materially. It is stronger than “finite linear constraints are too weak.” It says even if you search for a canonical linear local operator relation on \(q\), there is no room left: after passing to the quotient by \(\Pi_6\), everything collapses to \(q^{(7)}\), i.e. to the already-universal direct slice \(\phi=Aq^{(7)}\). This is precisely why the notes say the next viable theorem must either fix the seven-dimensional gauge, or use an order-\(\ge 7\) law with extra coupling, or use a nonlinear / non-gauge-invariant relation. 

That gives a very concrete new frontier:

\[
\boxed{
\text{to get any new theorem, you must do one of three things:}
}
\]

First, fix the full \(\Pi_6\) gauge by extracting seven independent boundary/matching conditions from genuinely external mixed/canonical structure. The notes explicitly identify this as one of the only live possibilities. 

Second, derive an order-\(\ge 7\) provenance law for \(q\) that is not just a disguised restatement of
\[
\phi=Aq^{(7)}.
\]
Again, this is exactly one of the surviving options named in the notes. 

Third, find a nonlinear or non-gauge-invariant provenance relation, for example something comparing \(q\) across blocks or coupling it to external canonical data in a way not preserved by \(q\mapsto q+P\). The notes also single this out as the first type of relation not killed by the current obstruction. 

That also clarifies what to stop doing. The current materials already say:

- arbitrary canonical quotient-septic geometry is still locally free once the lower one-pair data are fixed, so “route 2 + arbitrary \(\Delta_7\)” is dead; turn50file4
- the explicit direct slice \(\phi=Aq^{(7)}\) is fully universal on each generic one-pair block; turn52file1
- even finite linear provenance/matching conditions on \(q\) are too weak. turn52file3

So the only honest local attack left is not “find another linear identity on \(q\).” It is either:

\[
\boxed{
\text{extract seven external conditions that fix the }\Pi_6\text{ gauge,}
}
\]
or
\[
\boxed{
\text{find a genuinely external order-}7\text{ or nonlinear law.}
}
\]

My recommendation for the very next push is the first one, because it is the sharpest test of whether Attack A still has life:

Try to identify seven independent block-boundary quantities from the mixed/canonical package that are invariantly attached to the actual RH branch and determine
\[
q(h_0),q'(h_0),\dots,q^{(6)}(h_0)
\]
at one basepoint of a generic block. If that can be done, then the gauge is gone and a lower-order law for \(q\) becomes meaningful again. If it cannot be done, then the pointwise linear route is truly exhausted, and only nonlinear / order-\(\ge 7\) / whole-block laws remain. That is exactly the frontier encoded in the notes. 

So the attack has sharpened to this:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Next theorem target: gauge-fixing lemma for the direct provenance variable }q.
}
\]

If you want, I’ll attack that directly next: try to mine the mixed/canonical package for seven independent boundary conditions that would kill the \(\Pi_6\) freedom.

\[
F\bigl(h,B(h),q(h),q'(h),\dots,q^{(r)}(h)\bigr)=0
\]
uses only the current direct-slice package and is invariant under the natural gauge
\[
q\mapsto q+P,\qquad P\in \Pi_6,
\]
then the law is vacuous. The argument is: the \(\Pi_6\)-gauge is surjective on the first seven jet coordinates at a point, so gauge invariance kills dependence on \(q,\dots,q^{(6)}\); then because
\[

\]
and \(\phi\) is fully universal on the block, the remaining tail jets are also arbitrary, forcing the law to be empty. The notes spell this out and then summarize the consequence: the direct-slice lane is exhausted for all universal pointwise finite-order laws on a block. turn56file1

A useful corollary is the sharper operator-level statement:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{No nontrivial canonical linear differential law for }q\textbf{ of order }\le 6\textbf{ can exist at the current package level.}

The notes give the proof idea directly. If a linear differential operator
\[
T=\sum_{k=0}^r b_k(h)\partial_h^k,\qquad r\le 6,
\]
were canonical for the current package, it would have to be invariant under \(q\mapsto q+P\) for all \(P\in\Pi_6\), hence annihilate every polynomial of degree at most \(6\). Evaluating on shifted monomials then forces all coefficients \(b_k\) to vanish. So any order-\(\le 6\) local linear provenance law is dead.

The notes already prove that even after any finite family of linear provenance or matching conditions on \(q\), the direct slice
\[

\]
still realizes bitangent, four-secant, and same-slope recurrence geometry, and they summarize the strategic consequence as: finite collections of pointwise conditions are spent; the next live lane has to be continuum-strength or use genuinely external non-universal fields. turn56file4

\[

\text{all universal pointwise finite-order laws are spent;}

The notes say exactly that in two forms: first, after the vacuity theorem, the only live possibilities left are a genuinely nonlocal law or a pointwise law using external non-universal mixed/canonical fields; second, the “next live target” in the draft is to hybridize the moving shear

with higher non-universal data such as \([A_7^{\mathfrak f}]\) or \(\Delta_7\). turn54file2

_Thought for 53s_

Yes. With the new Attack B handback, the attack is now much sharper.

The real lesson is that the residual mixed corner has been compressed as far as universal finite-order transport geometry will take it: on \(\{S=0\}\cap\{K_v=0\}\), the branch is involutive/quotient-diagonal, every parity-normalized finite transport jet descends to \(u=t^2\), the quartic–sextic rung has rank-one finite transport state, and there is no third local reset in any finite descended transport state. That immediately changes what Attack A should target. The right local chart near a close bad two-point branch is not the naive diagonal \((h_1,h_2)=(h,h)\), but the collision-cancellation locus
\[
\delta=h_2-h_1=0,\qquad \lambda=-\frac{a_2}{a_1}=1,
\]
because the cubic balance forces \(a_1+a_2\approx 0\) when \(h_1\approx h_2\) on a good patch with \(c\neq 0\). In the blown-up chart
\[
m=\frac{h_1+h_2}{2},\qquad \delta=h_2-h_1,\qquad \mu=\lambda-1,
\]
the first-order source direction is the projective datum
\[
\Theta_{m,\theta}=\cos\theta\,D_m+\sin\theta\,D_m',
\]
so the next theorem should be phrased against this cancellation chart, not the old diagonal-merger chart.  

So the next attack I would make is this:

\[
\boxed{\textbf{Blown-up collision-functoriality theorem}}
\]

Take the actual corrected two-atom cubic/quintic/septic package on a good patch \(J\Subset\{c\neq 0\}\), move into the blow-up variables \((m,\rho,\theta)\) with
\[
(\mu,\delta)=\rho(\cos\theta,\sin\theta),
\]
and ask whether, after the natural projectivization/normalization, the corrected witnesses admit limits as \(\rho\to 0\) that depend only on \((m,\theta)\), equivalently only on the projective source direction \(\Theta_{m,\theta}\). That is exactly the replacement for the stale old target “prove \(O(\rho^2)\) on the diagonal chart.” The new question is whether the first blow-up law is functorial in the projective direction.  

Why this is the right theorem is that it would bridge directly to the honest order-7 obstruction. The new handback is explicit that the septic datum that really matters is not raw order-7 equality, but the quotient class
\[
[A_7^{\mathfrak f}]\in \mathfrak f/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]
And it also says that if two corrected germs agree through cubic and quintic order and differ only by an odd reparametrization plus the already-quotiented lower gauge, then the septic quotient defect vanishes formally. So the real open theorem is not “prove septic equality”; it is “prove same reduced image germ at coincidence,” or concretely prove collision-functoriality of the corrected block triple on the cancellation locus. If you get that, the quotient-septic obstruction collapses formally afterward.   

So my attack plan from here is:

First, formulate a precise blown-up limit object
\[
\mathcal B(m,\theta)
\]
for the corrected block triple on the cancellation chart. Second, prove it is well-defined up to the known odd-reparametrization and lower scalar/value gauge. Third, show that this already forces “same reduced image germ at coincidence.” Fourth, conclude that the transverse order-7 quotient class \([A_7^{\mathfrak f}]\) must vanish on the collision limit. At that point the only remaining possibility would be that the first relational two-atom invariant is not captured by the corrected block triple at all, which would be a much narrower and cleaner residual burden than before.  

So the attack has now become very concrete: I am no longer trying to squeeze one more contradiction out of the universal route-2 package. I am trying to prove that the corrected two-atom package has a blow-up functoriality law on the cancellation locus, because that is the first place the new handback indicates a genuinely non-universal relational invariant can appear. If you want, the next turn I’ll write the theorem in exact math form and sketch the proof architecture lemma by lemma.

\[

\]
because cubic balance forces \(a_1+a_2\approx 0\) when \(h_1\approx h_2\). In blow-up variables
\[
m=\frac{h_1+h_2}{2},\qquad \delta=h_2-h_1,\qquad \mu=\lambda-1,
\]
the two-atom source has the first-order expansion
\[
D_{h_1}-\lambda D_{h_2}
=

\]
so after polar blow-up \((\mu,\delta)=\rho(\cos\theta,\sin\theta)\), the effective projective source direction is

If that holds, then two collision paths with the same \((m,\theta)\) produce the same reduced image germ at coincidence. vanishes. In other words, the transverse quotient-septic obstruction disappears formally once collision-functoriality / same reduced image germ is known. turn61file5
