Now make the key package-level hypothesis:

> After projectivization on the cancellation chart, the corrected cubic and quintic witnesses have leading blow-up limits depending only on the projective source direction \(\Theta_{m,\theta}\), and those limits are exactly the one-pair cubic/quintic functionals evaluated on that direction.

In concrete terms, this means the leading blown-up cubic witness is
\[
C(m,\theta)=\cos\theta\,c(m)+\sin\theta\,c'(m),
\]
and the leading blown-up quintic witness is
\[
K(m,\theta)=\cos\theta\,A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)+\sin\theta\,(A_5^{\mathfrak f})'(m).
\]

This is the first real theorem target. If it is true, then the local geometry collapses immediately.

Indeed, cubic cancellation forces
\[
C(m,\theta)=0.
\]
Since \(c(m)\neq 0\) on the good patch, this determines a unique projective direction:
\[
(\cos\theta:\sin\theta)=(c'(m): -\,c(m)).
\]
Equivalently, the only cubic-cancelling direction is
\[
\Theta_m^{\mathrm{can}}=c'(m)\,D_m-c(m)\,D_m'.
\]

Now evaluate the quintic witness on that same direction:
\[
K\bigl(m,\theta_{\mathrm{can}}(m)\bigr)
=
c'(m)\,A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)-c(m)\,(A_5^{\mathfrak f})'(m)
=
-\,M(m),
\]
where
\[
M(m)=c(m)(A_5^{\mathfrak f})'(m)-c'(m)A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m).
\]

So on \(J\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\}\),
\[
C(m,\theta)=0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
K(m,\theta)\neq 0.
\]

That is the core obstruction.

So the conditional theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Conditional tangent-direction obstruction.}
}
\]

If the corrected cubic/quintic blow-up limits on the cancellation chart are functorial in the projective source direction \(\Theta_{m,\theta}\), then no close cancelling bad two-point branch can exist on any good patch \(J\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\}\).

That is much stronger than the earlier vague attack. It says the whole local problem reduces to one explicit canonical direction, and quintic kills it by the determinant \(M\). This is exactly the place the handback hinted that one-pair geometry re-enters via the linear independence of \((c,A_5^{\mathfrak f})\) and its derivative. 

What this changes strategically is important.

The next package-level theorem to attack is not yet “same reduced image germ” in full order \(7\). It is first:

\[
\boxed{
\text{projective blow-up functoriality at cubic/quintic order.}
}
\]

If that is proved, then good patches are already dead by the computation above, and septic becomes secondary there. Order \(7\) would then be needed only for the stronger global coincidence/functoriality story, or for zones where the lower-order determinant \(M\) is allowed to vanish.

So the refined order of battle is:

First, prove that the blown-up corrected cubic witness depends only on \(\Theta_{m,\theta}\) and equals the induced one-pair cubic functional.

Second, prove the analogous statement for quintic.

Third, conclude that the cubic-cancelling projective direction is forced to be
\[
\Theta_m^{\mathrm{can}}=c'(m)\,D_m-c(m)\,D_m',
\]
and that quintic on that direction is \(-M(m)\), hence nonzero on a good patch.

Only after that should we spend serious effort on the quotient-septic class
\[
[A_7^{\mathfrak f}] \in \mathfrak f/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f},
\]
because if the cubic/quintic blow-up functoriality theorem holds, septic is no longer the first local obstruction on good patches. turn57file2

So my honest continuation is: the best live theorem target is now a **blown-up cubic/quintic functoriality theorem**, and if it lands, the good-patch local two-point problem collapses immediately by the explicit determinant computation above.

The next thing I would do is write that theorem in exact proposition form, with the blow-up hypotheses separated cleanly from the determinant conclusion.

## Assistant (2026-04-21 17:21:28)

I’m checking the current draft language around the cancellation chart and the \(M\)-determinant so I can push from the handback to the next actual theorem, rather than just restating the strategy.

_Thought for 1m 0s_

Here is the next real push, and I think it is stronger than the earlier qualitative slogan.

The new handback does not just suggest the right chart. It suggests a **quantitative local exclusion theorem** on good patches, provided the corrected cubic/quintic witnesses admit the right blow-up limits. The key point is that the cubic-killing direction is not merely unique; it is **transverse**, and the quintic witness is uniformly separated from zero there. That makes the local obstruction robust.  

Work on a compact good patch
\[
J\Subset \{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\},
\qquad
M:=c(A_5^{\mathfrak f})'-c'A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]
On the cancellation chart
\[
m=\frac{h_1+h_2}{2},\qquad
\delta=h_2-h_1,\qquad
\mu=\lambda-1,
\qquad
(\mu,\delta)=\rho(\cos\theta,\sin\theta),
\]
the first-order source direction is
\[
\Theta_{m,\theta}=\cos\theta\,D_m+\sin\theta\,D_m'.
\]
The handback already identifies this as the correct local datum near a close cancelling branch.  

Now assume the corrected cubic and quintic witnesses have projectivized blow-up limits depending only on \((m,\theta)\), and that these limits are the one-pair functionals on the projective source direction:
\[
C(m,\theta)=\cos\theta\,c(m)+\sin\theta\,c'(m),
\]
\[
K(m,\theta)=\cos\theta\,A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)+\sin\theta\,(A_5^{\mathfrak f})'(m).
\]
This is exactly the blow-up functoriality input we were circling around. It is not proved yet, but it is the right theorem target. 

From there, the geometry is extremely rigid.

Because \(c(m)\neq 0\) on \(J\), the cubic equation
\[
C(m,\theta)=0
\]
has a unique projective solution:
\[
(\cos\theta:\sin\theta)=(c'(m):-c(m)).
\]
If we normalize to the unit circle, this is
\[
\cos\theta_*=\frac{c'}{\sqrt{c^2+(c')^2}},
\qquad
\sin\theta_*=-\frac{c}{\sqrt{c^2+(c')^2}}.
\]
So the canonical cubic-killing direction is
\[
\Theta_m^{\mathrm{can}}=c'(m)\,D_m-c(m)\,D_m'.
\]

Now differentiate \(C\) in \(\theta\):
\[
\partial_\theta C(m,\theta)
=
-\,c(m)\sin\theta + c'(m)\cos\theta.
\]
At the cubic-killing direction \(\theta=\theta_*(m)\),
\[
\partial_\theta C(m,\theta_*(m))
=
\pm \sqrt{c(m)^2+c'(m)^2}.
\]
Since \(c\neq 0\) on \(J\), this is never zero. In particular, the cubic-killing direction is a **simple root in \(\theta\)**, uniformly transverse on compact \(J\). That already matters: any actual corrected cubic witness close to the model blow-up will have a unique nearby zero direction.

Now evaluate the quintic model at the same direction:
\[
K(m,\theta_*(m))
=
\frac{c'(m)A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)-c(m)(A_5^{\mathfrak f})'(m)}
{\sqrt{c(m)^2+c'(m)^2}}
=
-\frac{M(m)}{\sqrt{c(m)^2+c'(m)^2}}.
\]
Since \(M\neq 0\) on \(J\), this is uniformly nonzero on compact \(J\). So the quintic witness has a definite gap at the unique cubic-killing direction.

This gives the sharper local statement:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Conditional uniform tangent-direction exclusion.}
}
\]

If the corrected cubic/quintic witnesses converge uniformly on compact good patches to the projective limits \(C\) and \(K\) above, then for sufficiently small \(\rho\) they cannot vanish simultaneously. Hence no close cancelling bad two-point branch can exist on \(J\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\}\).

Why this is stronger than the earlier version: it is not merely “there is a unique cubic-killing direction and quintic is nonzero there.” It says the obstruction is **stable under perturbation**, because:
- the cubic zero is simple in \(\theta\),
- the quintic gap there is uniform,
- so nearby corrected witnesses inherit the same exclusion for small enough blow-up scale.

That means the only real missing input is not some mysterious global geometry. It is a precise analytic package statement:

\[
\boxed{
\text{uniform blow-up asymptotics of the corrected cubic/quintic witnesses on the cancellation chart.}
}
\]

This also clarifies the role of order \(7\). On good patches, if this cubic/quintic blow-up functoriality theorem is true, then order \(7\) is not needed for local exclusion at all. Septic only re-enters for the stronger coincidence/functoriality story, where the honest datum is the quotient class
\[
[A_7^{\mathfrak f}]\in \mathfrak f/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f},
\]
and where same reduced image germ would force that class to vanish formally. The handback says exactly that cubic/quintic are already decisive locally if the right state-locality/functoriality holds, while septic is the transverse obstruction for the stronger global route.  

So the attack is now very concentrated. The next theorem to prove is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Blow-up cubic/quintic asymptotics theorem.}
}
\]

Namely: after projectivization on the cancellation chart, the corrected cubic and quintic witnesses admit uniform asymptotic expansions
\[
\mathcal C_3(m,\rho,\theta)=\rho\,C(m,\theta)+o(\rho),
\qquad
\mathcal C_5(m,\rho,\theta)=\rho\,K(m,\theta)+o(\rho),
\]
uniformly on compact good patches.

If that lands, the good-patch local two-point problem is essentially over by the transversality-and-gap argument above.

So the present frontier is no longer vague. It is this very specific analytic question: do the corrected cubic/quintic witnesses linearize on the cancellation blow-up to the one-pair functionals on \(\Theta_{m,\theta}\)? If yes, good patches die immediately.

_Thought for 17s_

Here is the next real push.

I think the strongest local theorem now in reach is not just “functoriality on the blow-up chart,” but a more precise **stability-by-transversality** statement. The new handback already gives almost all the geometry needed for it: on a good patch
\[
J\Subset \{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\},
\qquad
M:=c(A_5^{\mathfrak f})'-c'A_5^{\mathfrak f},
\]
the cancellation chart
\[
m=\frac{h_1+h_2}{2},\qquad \delta=h_2-h_1,\qquad \mu=\lambda-1,\qquad (\mu,\delta)=\rho(\cos\theta,\sin\theta)
\]
has first-order source direction
\[
\Theta_{m,\theta}=\cos\theta\,D_m+\sin\theta\,D_m',
\]
and the one-pair cubic/quintic functionals on that direction are
\[
C(m,\theta)=\cos\theta\,c(m)+\sin\theta\,c'(m),
\]
\[
K(m,\theta)=\cos\theta\,A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)+\sin\theta\,(A_5^{\mathfrak f})'(m).
\]
The handback’s determinant computation then shows that the unique cubic-killing direction is
\[
\Theta_m^{\mathrm{can}}=c'(m)\,D_m-c(m)\,D_m',
\]
and at that direction
\[
K(m,\theta_*(m))
=
-\frac{M(m)}{\sqrt{c(m)^2+c'(m)^2}},
\]
so quintic is uniformly separated from zero on compact good patches. 

The part I can sharpen now is this: the cubic root is not just unique, it is **uniformly simple**, and that means any sufficiently accurate corrected blow-up model inherits a unique nearby cubic zero direction, where quintic still stays away from zero. So the actual theorem target becomes a perturbative one.

Concretely, suppose the corrected cubic and quintic witnesses on the cancellation chart satisfy uniform first-order asymptotics
\[
\mathcal C_3(m,\rho,\theta)=\rho\,C(m,\theta)+o(\rho),
\qquad
\mathcal C_5(m,\rho,\theta)=\rho\,K(m,\theta)+o(\rho),
\]
uniformly for \(m\in J\) and \(\theta\in S^1\). Then:

First, because
\[
\partial_\theta C(m,\theta_*(m))
=
\pm\sqrt{c(m)^2+c'(m)^2},
\]
and \(c\neq 0\) on \(J\), there is a uniform lower bound
\[
|\partial_\theta C(m,\theta_*(m))|\ge \eta>0
\qquad (m\in J).
\]

Second, because \(M\neq 0\) on \(J\), there is a uniform quintic gap
\[
|K(m,\theta_*(m))|\ge \kappa>0
\qquad (m\in J).
\]

Third, by the implicit-function theorem plus uniform convergence, for sufficiently small \(\rho\) the corrected cubic witness \(\mathcal C_3\) has a unique zero
\[
\theta=\theta_\rho(m)
\]
near \(\theta_*(m)\), and
\[
\theta_\rho(m)-\theta_*(m)\to 0
\]
uniformly on \(J\).

Fourth, evaluating the corrected quintic witness at that corrected cubic-killing direction gives
\[
\frac{1}{\rho}\mathcal C_5(m,\rho,\theta_\rho(m))
\to
K(m,\theta_*(m))
\]
uniformly on \(J\), hence for all sufficiently small \(\rho\),
\[
\mathcal C_5(m,\rho,\theta_\rho(m))\neq 0.
\]

So simultaneous vanishing of corrected cubic and quintic is impossible for sufficiently small blow-up scale. That rules out close cancelling bad two-point cores on \(J\).

This is a stronger local reduction than before because it isolates the exact missing analytic input:

\[
\boxed{
\text{uniform first-order blow-up asymptotics of the corrected cubic/quintic witnesses.}
}
\]

Not vague functoriality. Not a full package theorem. Just this specific asymptotic statement.

So the clean next theorem target is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Blow-up asymptotics theorem on good patches.}
}
\]

On each compact \(J\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\}\), the corrected cubic and quintic witnesses admit uniform first-order expansions on the cancellation chart with leading terms \(C(m,\theta)\) and \(K(m,\theta)\) above.

If that is proved, the good-patch close-core lane dies immediately by the transversality/gap argument.

There is also a useful meta-conclusion here. This pushes septic even further out of the local picture. On good patches, order \(7\) is no longer the first obstruction if cubic/quintic blow-up asymptotics hold. Septic only remains relevant for the stronger global coincidence/functoriality route, where the honest datum is the quotient class
\[
[A_7^{\mathfrak f}]\in \mathfrak f/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f},
\]
and same reduced image germ would force its collapse formally. The handback already makes exactly that distinction. turn57file2

So my attack from here is:

1. Prove the uniform cancellation-chart asymptotics for corrected cubic.
2. Prove the same for corrected quintic.
3. Apply the uniform simple-root + uniform gap argument above.
4. Conclude: no close cancelling bad two-point cores on compact good patches.

That is now the sharpest local theorem lane I see.

## Assistant (2026-04-21 18:39:40)

_Thought for 7s_

Here is the full write-up of the attack as I now understand it.

The big picture is that the live two-point problem has split into three lanes, and only one of them still looks locally dangerous.

First, there is the **strong finite-order source/package merger route**: prove that the actual corrected two-atom package has the right functoriality/merger behavior on coincident atoms. If that holds, the quadratic interaction factorization becomes formal. Second, there is the **exact quotient-diagonal route** on the mixed residual exact fixed-shear corner \(\{S=0\}\cap\{K_v=0\}\): there the local branch is now highly compressed by involution/quotient descent. Third, there is the **cancellation-chart route** for close bad two-point cores on good patches \(J\Subset\{c\neq 0\}\): this is now the sharpest local theorem target. 

## 1. What is genuinely established on the mixed residual exact fixed-shear corner

On the residual exact fixed-shear slice, the branch is involutive/quotient-diagonal. The transport scalar
\[
Q(t):=\frac{J_{u_5}(t)}{J_\lambda(t)}
\]
is even:
\[
Q(t)=\widehat Q(t^2).
\]
So the natural quotient variable is
\[
u=t^2.
\]
This is already a major reduction: the local residual branch is no longer a free two-sided \(t\)-germ. turn57file1

A stronger theorem-level gain is the finite transport-jet quotient descent. Define parity-normalized transport jets
\[
\Theta_k(t):=t^{-(k\bmod 2)}Q^{(k)}(t),\qquad k\ge 0.
\]
Because \(Q\) is even, each \(\Theta_k\) is again even analytic, hence descends:
\[
\Theta_k(t)=\widetilde\Theta_k(t^2).
\]
So every finite parity-normalized transport jet is quotient-visible. turn57file1

On the first surviving residual rung,
\[
(m,n)=(4,6)\iff (r,e)=(2,0),
\]
one has
\[
\widehat Q'(0)=\widehat{\mathcal D}(0)\neq 0,
\]
so \(\widehat Q\) is a local coordinate in the quotient variable \(u\). Therefore every descended jet is locally an analytic function of \(Q\) alone:
\[
\Theta_k(t)=F_k(Q(t)).
\]
This is the **rank-one transport-state theorem**: on the quartic–sextic rung, the whole finite quotient-visible transport state has local rank \(1\). turn57file1

A clean corollary is the **no finite-order hidden reset theorem**. If
\[
\mathcal T_N(t):=(\Theta_0(t),\dots,\Theta_N(t)),
\]
then on the quartic–sextic rung
\[
\mathcal T_N(t_1)=\mathcal T_N(t_2)\quad\Longrightarrow\quad t_2=\pm t_1.
\]
So the only local duplication in any finite descended transport state is the known involution pair \(t\leftrightarrow -t\); there is no third local reset. This rules out a whole class of hidden finite-order state mechanisms. turn57file1

### Structural finding
If the exact fixed-shear residual corner is still live, the obstruction cannot come from:
- a second local transport parameter on the quartic–sextic rung,
- a hidden third reset in any finite descended transport state,
- or any mechanism built only from the separate descended one-atom transport states, assuming the natural merger law. turn57file1

That is a real theorem-level compression of the residual mixed corner.

## 2. What is only conditional there

There are strong conditional closures, but they remain conditional.

If the corrected cubic/quintic residual defects are analytic functionals of a finite descended transport state and vanish on the diagonal state, then
\[
E_{12}^{(3)}(t),\,E_{12}^{(5)}(t)=O(t^2),
\]
hence, because
\[
h(t)-h(-t)=2h'(0)t+O(t^3),
\]
one gets
\[
E_{12}^{(3)},\,E_{12}^{(5)}=O((h_1-h_2)^2).
\]
That is exactly the scale needed for the existing good-patch defect-closeness exclusion. turn57file1

More strongly, if the full corrected two-pair package is state-local in the two individual descended one-atom states and satisfies the natural diagonal merger law
\[
\mathfrak P_2(a_1,a_2;Y,Y)=(a_1+a_2)\mathfrak F(Y),
\]
then on the involutive branch the interaction remainder vanishes identically. turn57file1

### Negative finding
These are not yet unconditional theorems about the actual package. So they reduce the burden sharply, but they do not yet fully close the corner. The remaining gap is exactly whether the actual corrected package belongs to one of these state-local classes. turn57file1

## 3. The key correction: the right local chart is the cancellation chart, not the naive diagonal

Near a genuine close bad two-point branch on a good patch \(J\Subset\{c\neq 0\}\), the relevant limiting locus is not the ordinary diagonal \((h_1,h_2)=(h,h)\) with arbitrary total amplitude. It is the **collision-cancellation locus**
\[
\delta:=h_2-h_1=0,\qquad \lambda:=-\frac{a_2}{a_1}=1.
\]
Why: the cubic identity forces
\[
a_1c(h_1)+a_2c(h_2)\approx 0,
\]
so when \(h_1\approx h_2\) and \(c\neq 0\), one must have \(a_1+a_2\approx 0\), equivalently \(\lambda\approx 1\). Thus the combined source tends to zero, not to a one-atom diagonal source. That means the old diagonal-merger chart was aimed at the wrong base point. turn57file2

The correct local coordinates are
\[
m=\frac{h_1+h_2}{2},\qquad \delta=h_2-h_1,\qquad \mu=\lambda-1.
\]
Then the two-atom source expands as
\[
D_{h_1}-\lambda D_{h_2}
=
-\mu\,D_m-\delta\,D_m'+O\!\bigl((|\mu|+|\delta|)^2\bigr).
\]
After polar blow-up
\[
(\mu,\delta)=\rho(\cos\theta,\sin\theta),
\]
the effective first-order source direction is the projective datum
\[
\Theta_{m,\theta}:=\cos\theta\,D_m+\sin\theta\,D_m'.
\]
This is the right local datum near a close cancelling bad branch. turn57file2

### Structural finding
The live local two-point problem is not “prove \(O(\rho^2)\) on the diagonal chart.” It is to understand the **first blow-up law** of the corrected witnesses near \((\mu,\delta)=(0,0)\), and whether that law depends only on the projective direction \(\Theta_{m,\theta}\). turn57file2

## 4. The sharpest local theorem target: blown-up cubic/quintic functoriality

This is now, in my view, the best local attack.

Assume that after projectivization on the cancellation chart, the corrected cubic and quintic witnesses admit leading blow-up limits depending only on the projective source direction \(\Theta_{m,\theta}\), and that these limits are exactly the one-pair cubic/quintic functionals on that direction:
\[
C(m,\theta)=\cos\theta\,c(m)+\sin\theta\,c'(m),
\]
\[
K(m,\theta)=\cos\theta\,A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)+\sin\theta\,(A_5^{\mathfrak f})'(m).
\]

Then cubic cancellation forces
\[
C(m,\theta)=0.
\]
Since \(c(m)\neq 0\) on a good patch, this determines a unique projective direction:
\[
(\cos\theta:\sin\theta)=(c'(m):-c(m)).
\]
Equivalently, the unique cubic-killing direction is
\[
\Theta_m^{\mathrm{can}}=c'(m)\,D_m-c(m)\,D_m'.
\]

Now evaluate the quintic witness there:
\[
K(m,\theta_{\mathrm{can}}(m))
=
c'(m)A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)-c(m)(A_5^{\mathfrak f})'(m)
=
-\,M(m),
\]
where
\[
M(m)=c(m)(A_5^{\mathfrak f})'(m)-c'(m)A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m).
\]
So on a good patch
\[
J\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\},
\]
one gets
\[
C(m,\theta)=0\quad\Longrightarrow\quad K(m,\theta)\neq 0.
\]
That means cubic and quintic cannot vanish simultaneously. turn57file2

This can be sharpened further by a transversality argument. The cubic zero is uniformly simple because
\[
\partial_\theta C(m,\theta)
=
-\,c(m)\sin\theta+c'(m)\cos\theta,
\]
and at the cubic-killing direction,
\[
\partial_\theta C(m,\theta_*(m))
=
\pm \sqrt{c(m)^2+c'(m)^2},
\]
which is uniformly bounded away from zero on compact \(J\Subset\{c\neq 0\}\). Meanwhile the quintic value there is uniformly bounded away from zero because \(M\neq 0\) on \(J\). So if the corrected witnesses satisfy uniform blow-up asymptotics
\[
\mathcal C_3(m,\rho,\theta)=\rho\,C(m,\theta)+o(\rho),
\qquad
\mathcal C_5(m,\rho,\theta)=\rho\,K(m,\theta)+o(\rho),
\]
uniformly on compact good patches, then for sufficiently small \(\rho\) they cannot vanish simultaneously. This gives a robust local exclusion. This transversality/gap argument is my own sharpening of the handback, based on the same \(C,K,M\) structure. The handback directly supports the underlying determinant computation and the role of the good patch. turn57file2

### Conditional local theorem
If the corrected cubic/quintic witnesses linearize on the cancellation blow-up to the one-pair functionals \(C\) and \(K\), then no close cancelling bad two-point branch can exist on any compact good patch
\[
J\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\}.
\]

### Goodie
On good patches, septic is not the first local obstruction anymore. If this cubic/quintic blow-up functoriality holds, quintic already kills the unique cubic-cancelling direction. Septic is only needed for the stronger global coincidence/functoriality route, or near the exceptional set \(M=0\). This division of labor is strongly suggested by the new handback. turn57file2

## 5. The honest order-7 datum

The honest septic datum is not raw order-7 equality of representatives. It is the quotient class
\[
[A_7^{\mathfrak f}]\in \mathfrak f/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]
The handback makes two key points:

First, once two corrected germs agree through cubic and quintic order and differ only by an odd reparametrization plus the already-quotiented lower scalar/value gauge, the order-7 mismatch is automatically a multiple of \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\), so the septic quotient defect vanishes.

Second, cubic/quintic merger alone does **not** force that odd-reparametrization comparability. So the transverse quotient-septic class is the exact remaining obstruction. turn57file2

Therefore the honest order-7 theorem target is not “prove septic equality.” It is one of the following:
- prove **same reduced image germ at coincidence**,
- or prove **collision-functoriality** of the corrected block triple on the collision/cancellation locus.

If that weaker functoriality theorem holds, then the septic quotient collapse becomes formal afterward. turn57file2

## 6. What is dead

A few negative findings are now pretty sharp.

The naive source-summed corrected-block route cannot prove the strong merger theorem. Along a weighted one-atom path, its extracted finite-order coefficients are even analytic in the source weight, so the required linear merger law cannot come from that model. That kills the earlier “obvious source-linear closure” route. 

Also, the mixed residual exact fixed-shear corner cannot be closed by any hidden mechanism inside the universal finite descended transport state alone. If anything is still live there, it has to come from the first relational/provenance-sensitive two-atom datum, or from non-finite-order dependence. turn57file1

And on the nonmixed/source-coupling side, the new two-point handoff strongly reinforces the conclusion already reached in the draft: do not spend cycles squeezing more out of the same universal scalar/discriminant package. Any surviving obstruction has to be genuinely non-universal and source-coupled. 

## 7. Clean summary of the current frontier

Here is the cleanest mathematical summary I can give.

### Established structural gains
On the residual exact fixed-shear corner \(\{S=0\}\cap\{K_v=0\}\):
\[
Q(t)=\widehat Q(t^2),
\]
every parity-normalized finite transport jet descends to \(u=t^2\), and on the quartic–sextic rung the whole finite quotient-visible transport state is locally rank \(1\). Hence no finite-order hidden reset survives beyond the involution symmetry. turn57file1

### Correct local chart
Near a close bad two-point core on a good patch, the right local chart is the collision-cancellation blow-up
\[
m=\frac{h_1+h_2}{2},\qquad
(\mu,\delta)=\rho(\cos\theta,\sin\theta),
\]
with projective source direction
\[
\Theta_{m,\theta}=\cos\theta\,D_m+\sin\theta\,D_m'.
\]
Not the naive diagonal. turn57file2

### Best local theorem target
Prove uniform blow-up asymptotics for the corrected cubic/quintic witnesses:
\[
\mathcal C_3(m,\rho,\theta)=\rho\,C(m,\theta)+o(\rho),
\qquad
\mathcal C_5(m,\rho,\theta)=\rho\,K(m,\theta)+o(\rho),
\]
with
\[
C(m,\theta)=\cos\theta\,c(m)+\sin\theta\,c'(m),
\]
\[
K(m,\theta)=\cos\theta\,A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)+\sin\theta\,(A_5^{\mathfrak f})'(m).
\]
If that holds, then on
\[
J\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\}
\]
there are no close cancelling bad two-point cores. This is the sharpest local attack I currently see. The \(C,K\) formulas and the role of \(M\) are directly grounded in the handback; the uniform asymptotics formulation is the natural precise theorem target that emerges from them. turn57file2

### Best stronger/global theorem target
Prove collision-functoriality / same reduced image germ at coincidence for the corrected block triple on the cancellation locus. If that holds, the quotient-septic obstruction
\[
[A_7^{\mathfrak f}]\in \mathfrak f/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\]
collapses formally. turn57file2

## 8. Bottom line

My current view is:

- The mixed residual exact fixed-shear corner has been compressed much further than before. Its universal finite-order transport geometry is essentially exhausted. turn57file1
- The right local close-core problem is now a blow-up problem on the cancellation chart, not a diagonal-merger problem. turn57file2
- On good patches \(J\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\}\), the next best theorem is **blown-up cubic/quintic functoriality**, because if that lands, close cancelling bad two-point cores are excluded locally. turn57file2
- Order \(7\) remains important, but as the **first genuinely relational quotient obstruction** after cubic/quintic and lower gauge are quotiented out; not as the first local obstruction on good patches. turn57file2

So the whole progress, in one sentence, is this:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The geometry is no longer the obstacle. The remaining burden is package-level: prove blow-up functoriality/state-locality on the cancellation chart, or isolate the first genuinely relational quotient-septic obstruction that survives after all lower universal structure is compressed away.}
}
\]

If you want, the next step is for me to turn this write-up into exact draft-ready theorem/remark blocks in LaTeX.

_Thought for 9s_

I reviewed both new summaries, and they are strong. The main thing they do is sharpen the two-point side from “the residual corner is constrained” to “the entire **analytic swap-invariant local** quadratic layer is probably harmless.” That is a real upgrade.  

Here is how I would classify them.

The most solid gains are these.

On the exact fixed-shear residual corner \(\{S=0\}\cap\{K_v=0\}\), the involutive/quotient picture is now much tighter: \(Q(t)=\widehat Q(t^2)\), every parity-normalized finite transport jet descends, and on the quartic–sextic rung the entire finite quotient-visible transport state has local rank \(1\). So there is no hidden second finite transport parameter and no third local reset in any finite descended transport state. That is a real theorem-level compression, not just a heuristic. 

The other major gain is the collision-cancellation chart. Using
\[
m=\frac{h_1+h_2}{2},\qquad \delta=h_2-h_1,\qquad \lambda=-\frac{a_2}{a_1},
\]
or equivalently the swap-compatible variable
\[
\omega=\frac{\lambda-1}{\lambda+1},
\]
is clearly the right local chart, and it linearizes the swap as
\[
(m,\omega,\delta)\mapsto (m,-\omega,-\delta).
\]
That matters because it kills the entire linear blow-up layer for any analytic swap-even defect vanishing on the collision locus. The factorization
\[
E(m,\omega,\delta)=\delta^2\,\mathcal H(m,\kappa,\delta^2),
\qquad
\kappa=\frac{2\omega}{\delta},
\]
is a genuinely useful structural normal form. 

The strongest new negative finding is the last one in the second summary: if the actual local obstruction were given by any **finite analytic swap-invariant local scalar** built from the cancellation variables, amplitude ratio, and descended transport state, then after passing to the \((\nu,\delta)\) chart with
\[
\nu=\log\Lambda,\qquad \Lambda=-\frac{a_2}{a_1},
\]
it would factor through the quadratic invariants
\[
\nu^2,\qquad \nu\delta,\qquad \delta^2,
\]
and hence would automatically be \(O((h_1-h_2)^2)\) once it vanishes on the diagonal state. That means the whole analytic swap-invariant local scalar class is now essentially squeezed out as a source of a live obstruction. This is a very strong and clean frontier statement. 

Where I would still be careful is with the closure wording.

Several of the strongest statements remain conditional on properties of the **actual corrected defects/package**: local analyticity in the collision chart, swap-evenness, collision vanishing, or broader state-locality hypotheses. Those are plausible and natural, but they are still assumptions on the real package, not yet theorems about it. So I would not yet write “the residual exact fixed-shear corner is closed” without qualification. The right phrasing is closer to: *any remaining obstruction must lie beyond the entire analytic swap-invariant local quadratic blow-up layer and beyond any finite descended transport-state mechanism*.  

That distinction matters because the summaries themselves are careful about the honest remaining possibilities: a surviving obstruction would have to be non-analytic in the cancellation chart, projective/blow-up-direction dependent without analytic extension, provenance-sensitive/discrete, or genuinely nonlocal / non-finite-order. That is exactly the right “what remains” statement. 

Strategically, these updates change the frontier in a way I think is very important.

Before, Attack A could still imagine that some local scalar/canonical refinement might close the residual corner. After these updates, that looks much less likely. The residual corner is now squeezed past:
- finite descended transport state,
- finite symmetric analytic relational corrections,
- and even the whole class of finite analytic swap-invariant local scalars. 

So the next live targets are narrower than before.

First, a **package theorem**: prove that the actual corrected cubic/quintic defects really do satisfy the local analyticity + swap-evenness + collision-vanishing hypotheses in the cancellation chart. If that lands, the residual exact fixed-shear corner is basically done by the quadratic harmlessness mechanism. 

Second, if that package theorem stalls, then the remaining obstruction cannot be an ordinary analytic local scalar anymore. So the next realistic attack is exactly what we were already converging to: the first genuinely relational / provenance-sensitive two-atom datum, likely expressed either as collision-functoriality / same reduced image germ, or as the transverse quotient-septic class
\[
[A_7^{\mathfrak f}] \in \mathfrak f/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]
That is also exactly how the second summary frames the global source-level route. 

So my verdict is:

These updates are good enough to import into the mathematical picture, but with the right stratification.

What I would treat as **proved structural gains**:
- quotient-diagonal/involutive residual corner,
- finite transport-jet quotient descent,
- rank-one finite transport state on the quartic–sextic rung,
- no third local reset,
- swap-even collision-chart factorization through \(\delta^2\mathcal H(m,\kappa,\delta^2)\),
- and the \((\nu,\delta)\) invariant-theory normal form for analytic swap-invariant local scalars.  

What I would treat as **conditional closures**:
- actual corrected cubic/quintic defects satisfying the collision-chart hypotheses imply \(O((h_1-h_2)^2)\) and hence exclusion on good patches,
- broader state-local / analytic relational models are also harmless under the same framework.  

What I would treat as the **new frontier**:
- the remaining obstruction, if any, must be non-analytic, nonlocal, or genuinely provenance-sensitive/two-atom-relational,
- so the strongest next attack is package-level collision functoriality or the quotient-septic obstruction class, not another universal local scalar argument. 

My practical recommendation is: yes, these should change the draft’s “current frontier” sections, but they should be inserted as a combination of theorem-level gains plus clearly marked conditional remarks, not as an unconditional full closure of the residual corner.

## The theorem I would now attack

Work on the collision-cancellation chart
\[
m=\frac{h_1+h_2}{2},\qquad
\delta=h_2-h_1,\qquad

\nu=\log\Lambda.

Under atom swap,

with \(Y\) an involution-invariant descended transport state has the normal form

F=G(m,\nu^2,\nu\delta,\delta^2,Y),

hence if it vanishes on the diagonal state it is automatically

therefore harmless for the good-patch defect-closeness argument.

## Why this is now the right attack

Because the other summaries already kill the plausible alternatives.

They show that on \(\{S=0\}\cap\{K_v=0\}\):

- the whole finite transport package is quotient-visible,
- on the quartic–sextic rung it has local rank \(1\),
- there is no third local reset,

  \[

That is why the next attack should be on the package itself.

## Concrete proof architecture

I would now try to prove the actual-package theorem in three lemmas.

### Lemma 1: analytic dependence before quotienting
Show that the corrected cubic/quintic witnesses are analytic functions of the raw two-atom parameters
\[
(a_1,h_1,a_2,h_2)
\]
away from the trivial singular charts, after whatever normalization/whitening/correction procedure defines them.

This is a construction-level statement: if the package is built from finite algebraic/differential operations on the corrected block data, this should be true.

### Lemma 2: pass to cancellation variables
Rewrite those analytic functions in the local coordinates
\[
m,\quad \delta,\quad \Lambda=-a_2/a_1,
\]
or better
\[
m,\quad \delta,\quad \nu=\log\Lambda.
\]
Near cancellation, \(\Lambda\approx 1\), so \(\nu\) is analytic. This should produce analytic representatives
\[
E_j=E_j(m,\nu,\delta).
\]

### Lemma 3: swap invariance and collision vanishing
Because the underlying two-atom defect should not depend on which atom is called “1” or “2,” one expects
\[
E_j(m,-\nu,-\delta)=E_j(m,\nu,\delta).
\]
And because on the collision-cancellation locus the two-atom source tends to zero to first order, the corrected defects should vanish there:
\[
E_j(m,0,0)=0.
\]

Once these three lemmas hold, the normal-form theorem from the summaries applies automatically, and you get
\[
E_j=O(\delta^2)=O((h_1-h_2)^2),
\]
which is exactly the exclusion scale already known. turn65file1

---

## The strongest mathematical reduction

So I think the sharpest reduction we have now is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Residual exact fixed-shear closure reduces to proving ordinary analytic local functoriality of the actual defects in the cancellation chart.}
}
\]

That is much better than before. It is no longer a vague request for “state-locality” or “some merger theorem.” It is this specific regularity/naturality claim.

---

## A stronger variant to test

There is an even more economical version.

The first summary shows that for any analytic swap-even defect in the \((m,\omega,\delta)\) chart,
\[
E=A(m)\omega^2+B(m)\omega\delta+C(m)\delta^2+O(4),
\]
hence
\[
E=\delta^2\,\mathcal H(m,\kappa,\delta^2).
\]
So one does not actually need the full \((\nu,\delta)\)-invariant-theory package to get started. It would already be enough to prove:

- analyticity in \((m,\omega,\delta)\),
- swap-evenness,
- collision vanishing.

Then the whole linear layer dies and the first surviving term is quadratic. On the involutive branch this already becomes quotient-visible:
\[
E(t)=\delta(t)^2\,\widetilde H(t^2).
\]
So even the weaker chart-analyticity theorem would be a real advance. 

---

## What I think is most likely true

My guess is:

- **swap invariance** should be formal,
- **collision vanishing** should be formal or nearly formal,
- the only genuinely delicate step is **analyticity in the cancellation chart** after all corrections/whitening/reparametrization choices are imposed.

So that is the part I would attack first.

## The next precise statement to prove

I would now aim at this:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Cancellation-chart analyticity proposition.}
}
\]

On a compact good patch \(J\Subset\{c\neq 0\}\), the actual corrected cubic and quintic defects admit analytic representatives
\[
E_{12}^{(3)}(m,\omega,\delta),\qquad E_{12}^{(5)}(m,\omega,\delta)
\]
near \((\omega,\delta)=(0,0)\), satisfy
\[
E_j(m,-\omega,-\delta)=E_j(m,\omega,\delta),
\qquad
E_j(m,0,0)=0,
\]
and therefore have the factorization
\[
E_j=\delta^2\,\mathcal H_j(m,\kappa,\delta^2),
\qquad \kappa=\frac{2\omega}{\delta}.
\]

If proved, this already pushes the corner beyond the entire quadratic blow-up layer in the sense of the new summary.

The next math attack is now very clear:

Do **not** hunt another geometric obstruction inside the already-compressed residual corner.

If that is true, the invariant-theory normal form from the new summaries wipes out the whole local analytic layer, and any remaining obstruction must be genuinely non-analytic, nonlocal, or provenance-sensitive.

That is where I would keep pushing next.

## 1. Reformulate the problem as extension across the collision set

On the cancellation chart,
\[
m=\frac{h_1+h_2}{2},\qquad
\delta=h_2-h_1,\qquad
\Lambda=-\frac{a_2}{a_1},\qquad
\omega=\frac{\Lambda-1}{\Lambda+1},
\]
the collision locus is
\[
(\omega,\delta)=(0,0).
\]
The summaries already show that if the corrected defects extend analytically to that point and are swap-even, then the whole linear layer dies and the first surviving term is quadratic:
\[
E=\delta^2\,\mathcal H(m,\kappa,\delta^2),
\qquad
\kappa=\frac{2\omega}{\delta},
\]
and on the involutive branch even that is quotient-visible. turn65file1

So the real remaining local question is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Do the actual corrected defects admit analytic extension to }(\omega,\delta)=(0,0)\textbf{?}
}
\]

That is more precise than “are they analytic local scalars?” The delicate point is not away from collision; it is whether the apparent singularities from whitening/normalization/reparametrization are removable at the cancellation point.

## 2. What would prove analyticity

A standard way to win this is to show three things.

First, the corrected cubic/quintic witnesses are analytic in the raw two-atom parameters on the open set where the construction is defined:
\[
(a_1,h_1,a_2,h_2).
\]

Second, after passing to
\[
(m,\omega,\delta),
\]
any denominators introduced by the construction vanish to no worse order than the numerators along the cancellation locus.

Third, the resulting boundedness/growth is compatible with analytic extension.

So the exact theorem I would now target is a removable-singularity proposition:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Removable cancellation singularity proposition.}
}
\]

After rewriting the actual corrected cubic and quintic defects in \((m,\omega,\delta)\), the apparent singularities at \((\omega,\delta)=(0,0)\) are removable, yielding analytic extensions
\[
E_{12}^{(3)}(m,\omega,\delta),\qquad
E_{12}^{(5)}(m,\omega,\delta).
\]

Once that is in hand, swap symmetry and collision vanishing should finish the local analytic layer automatically. turn65file1

## 3. Why this is the right next theorem

Because the summaries already rule out the alternatives.

If the defects extend analytically and are swap-even local scalars, the corner is pushed beyond the entire quadratic blow-up layer. On the quartic–sextic rung even that quadratic coefficient is just a function of \(Q\), so there is no real local room left. turn65file1

So if the corner is still live, one of the following must happen:

- the actual defects are **not analytically extendable** at cancellation,
- or they are not honest **swap-invariant local scalars**,
- or the obstruction is **nonlocal/provenance-sensitive** and not captured by any finite local scalar package. 

That means proving analytic extension is now a decisive fork in the road.

## 4. A sharper intermediate target

There is also a weaker theorem that may be easier and is already enough for exclusion.

You do not actually need full analytic extension first. It would already be enough to prove that the defects are **bounded by quadratic order** in the cancellation variables:
\[
E_{12}^{(j)}(m,\omega,\delta)=O(\omega^2+\omega\delta+\delta^2),
\qquad j=3,5,
\]
uniformly on compact good patches.

Why this helps: by swap symmetry, any odd linear part must cancel, so once you know there is no pole worse than first order, quadratic boundedness should follow. And that is already enough to get
\[
E_{12}^{(j)}=O((h_1-h_2)^2)
\]
along the involutive branch, which is the exclusion scale you want. So a weaker but still very useful next theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Quadratic boundedness on the cancellation chart.}
}
\]

This may be easier to prove directly from the construction than full analyticity.

## 5. What I think the package-level obstruction now looks like

If the removable-singularity / quadratic-boundedness theorem fails, then the obstruction is no longer a geometric one. It would mean the actual corrected package carries some non-removable dependence on the **direction of approach to cancellation**, i.e. truly projective blow-up data.

That would align perfectly with the other live route already identified in the summaries:
the first genuinely relational/provenance-sensitive datum, likely tied to collision functoriality or the quotient-septic class
\[
[A_7^{\mathfrak f}] \in \mathfrak f/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]
So even failure of analyticity would be informative: it would tell us exactly where the residual obstruction must live. 

## 6. The next concrete attack

So the next thing I would try to prove is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Near }(\omega,\delta)=(0,0),\textbf{ the corrected cubic/quintic defects have removable singularities.}
}
\]

And I would try to prove it by auditing the construction term-by-term:

- identify every denominator coming from whitening/normalization,
- expand each numerator along cancellation,
- show cancellation of all potentially dangerous first-order poles by the already-known symmetry/cubic-balance structure,
- conclude analytic extension, or at least quadratic boundedness.

That is now the sharpest local theorem lane I see.

The mathematical picture after this round is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Residual exact fixed-shear closure has been reduced to a regularity question for the actual corrected defects in the cancellation chart.}
}
\]

If the answer is yes, the whole analytic local layer is dead. If the answer is no, then the obstruction is forced into the genuinely projective/provenance-sensitive lane.

Here is the next honest push.

I think the right continuation is to turn the “regularity fork” into a **minimal-singularity theorem**. So if the residual exact fixed-shear corner is still live, the obstruction has to come from the **first non-analytic projective blow-up profile**. That can be formalized. turn65file1

## 1. The correct dichotomy

Work on the cancellation chart
\[
m=\frac{h_1+h_2}{2},\qquad
\delta=h_2-h_1,\qquad
\Lambda=-\frac{a_2}{a_1},\qquad
\omega=\frac{\Lambda-1}{\Lambda+1}.
\]
Under atom swap,
\[
(m,\omega,\delta)\mapsto (m,-\omega,-\delta).
\]

The summaries already show:

- if a corrected defect \(E\) is analytic in \((m,\omega,\delta)\),
- swap-even,
- and vanishes on the collision locus \((\omega,\delta)=(0,0)\),

then
\[
E(m,\omega,\delta)
=
A(m)\omega^2+B(m)\omega\delta+C(m)\delta^2
+O\!\big((|\omega|+|\delta|)^4\big),
\]
hence
\[
E=\delta^2\,\mathcal H(m,\kappa,\delta^2),
\qquad
\kappa=\frac{2\omega}{\delta}.
\]
So the whole linear layer dies, and the first surviving layer is quadratic and already projective. On the involutive exact fixed-shear branch, even that becomes quotient-visible; on the quartic–sextic rung, even its coefficient is locally a function of \(Q\) alone. turn65file1

Therefore the only way a local obstruction can survive is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{failure of ordinary analytic extension / quadratic boundedness at the collision point.}
}
\]

That is now the right fork.

## 2. Minimal non-analytic obstruction theorem

Let \(E(m,\omega,\delta)\) be an actual corrected cubic or quintic defect, defined on the punctured cancellation chart near \((\omega,\delta)=(0,0)\). Assume:

- \(E\) is locally bounded away from the collision point along non-collision configurations,
- \(E\) is swap-even:
  \[
  E(m,-\omega,-\delta)=E(m,\omega,\delta),
  \]
- \(E\) vanishes on the exact collision state in the sense relevant to the package.

Suppose \(E\) does **not** satisfy quadratic boundedness
\[
E=O(\omega^2+\omega\delta+\delta^2).
\]

Then there exists a smallest exponent
\[
\alpha\in [0,2)
\]
and a nonzero projective blow-up profile
\[
\mathcal P_\alpha(m,\kappa),
\qquad
\kappa=\frac{2\omega}{\delta},
\]
such that along suitable blow-up sequences
\[
(\omega,\delta)=\rho\Bigl(\frac{\kappa}{2},1\Bigr),\qquad \rho\to 0,
\]
one has
\[
\rho^{-\alpha}E(m,\omega,\delta)\to \mathcal P_\alpha(m,\kappa),
\]
and this profile is swap-even in the projective sense
\[
\mathcal P_\alpha(m,\kappa)=\mathcal P_\alpha(m,\kappa)
\]
since \((\omega,\delta)\mapsto(-\omega,-\delta)\) leaves \(\kappa\) unchanged.

This is not a full theorem yet because one needs a mild compactness/extraction argument for the rescaled family, but it is the right formal consequence: if analytic quadratic harmlessness fails, the first surviving obstruction must be a **nontrivial projective profile of order \(<2\)**.

That is already a big sharpening. It says the remaining obstruction is not some vague singularity — it is the first subquadratic homogeneous profile on the blow-up sphere.

## 3. Why this helps

Because now we can ask what such a profile would have to look like under the exact fixed-shear involutive compression.

On the involutive branch,
\[
(h_1,h_2)=(h(t),h(-t)),
\]
the summaries already show that any analytic swap-even defect becomes
\[
E(t)=\delta(t)^2\,\widetilde H(t^2),
\]
and on the quartic–sextic rung even
\[
E(t)=\delta(t)^2\,\mathcal G(Q(t)).
\]
So if a subquadratic profile survives, it cannot come from the ordinary descended analytic local law. It must come from a failure of analytic extension **before** one reaches that quotient-visible quadratic layer. turn65file1

Equivalently:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Any still-live local obstruction must be a genuinely projective singular profile, not an ordinary descended analytic scalar.}
}
\]

That is the sharpest negative statement I can now justify.

## 4. A concrete refinement: odd linear terms are impossible, so the first bad exponent is constrained

Because of swap-evenness, any genuine blow-up profile must be invariant under simultaneous sign reversal of \((\omega,\delta)\). That immediately kills odd homogeneous terms. So if there is a first nontrivial homogeneous profile, its order \(\alpha\) cannot be \(1\). More generally, any integer odd order is ruled out.

So the first bad exponent, if it exists, must be one of these types:

- a non-integer subquadratic exponent,
- or an even-but-subquadratic singular behavior arising from non-analytic dependence,
- or something logarithmic / non-power-like.

That is another useful narrowing:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the first surviving blow-up layer cannot be an ordinary linear tangent-direction law.}
}
\]

This is fully consistent with the first summary’s parity kill of the entire linear blown-up interaction layer. 

## 5. What the next proof should try to show

So the next actual theorem target is now even more precise than before.

Not just:

\[
\text{prove analyticity on the cancellation chart;}
\]

but:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{exclude subquadratic projective blow-up profiles for the actual corrected defects.}
}
\]

A good way to do that is to prove the weaker statement
\[
E=O(\rho^2)
\qquad
\text{with }
\rho\sim |\omega|+|\delta|
\]
uniformly on compact good patches. That already rules out every subquadratic profile and is enough for the good-patch closeness contradiction.

So the next concrete local theorem becomes:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Quadratic boundedness theorem on the cancellation chart.}
}
\]

If the actual corrected cubic/quintic defects satisfy
\[
E_{12}^{(j)}(m,\omega,\delta)=O(\omega^2+\omega\delta+\delta^2),
\qquad j=3,5,
\]
uniformly on compact good patches, then close cancelling bad two-point cores are excluded there.

This is weaker than full analyticity, but still decisive.

## 6. How to attack quadratic boundedness

I would now try to prove quadratic boundedness by a term-by-term audit of the construction.

The logic would be:

1. Express each corrected defect in the raw two-atom parameters \((a_1,h_1,a_2,h_2)\).
2. Rewrite in the cancellation variables \((m,\omega,\delta)\).
3. Identify every apparent singular denominator produced by normalization/whitening/reparametrization.
4. Show that the already-known cancellation identities force the numerator to vanish to matching order.
5. Use swap symmetry to kill any remaining first-order contribution.

If that works, one gets \(O(\rho^2)\) without needing the full analytic extension theorem.

## 7. What this means for the global frontier

This also clarifies the relation to the order-\(7\) route.

On good patches, if quadratic boundedness holds, cubic/quintic already exclude close cancelling bad cores. Then the quotient-septic class
\[
[A_7^{\mathfrak f}] \in \mathfrak f/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\]
is no longer the first local obstruction there. It remains relevant only for the stronger global coincidence/functoriality route or for exceptional loci where the lower-order good-patch determinant mechanism is unavailable. That matches the earlier handbacks very well. 

## Bottom line

The attack has now become:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Either the corrected defects are quadratically bounded on the cancellation chart, in which case the local analytic layer is dead,}
}
\]
or
\[
\boxed{
\text{there exists a first nontrivial subquadratic projective blow-up profile, and that is the only place a local obstruction can still hide.}
}
\]

That is the sharpest local fork I can currently see.

The next theorem I would try to prove is the quadratic boundedness theorem, because it is weaker than full analyticity but already enough to kill the good-patch local two-point lane.

_Thought for 5s_

Here is the next push.

I think the best move now is to extract a **minimal-bad-profile contradiction scheme** from the cancellation-chart fork. The last reduction says:

- either the corrected cubic/quintic defects are quadratically bounded on the cancellation chart, and then the good-patch local lane dies;
- or there is a first nontrivial subquadratic projective blow-up profile. turn65file1

So let us attack the second possibility directly.

## 1. Minimal bad profile setup

Write the corrected defect schematically as
\[
E(m,\omega,\delta),
\]
where \((m,\omega,\delta)\) are the cancellation variables. Assume we are on a compact good patch
\[
J\Subset \{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\}.
\]

Suppose quadratic boundedness fails. Then there exists a smallest exponent
\[
\alpha<2
\]
for which one can find a blow-up sequence
\[
(m_n,\omega_n,\delta_n)\to (m_*,0,0),
\qquad
\rho_n:=|\omega_n|+|\delta_n|\to 0,
\]
such that
\[
\rho_n^{-\alpha}E(m_n,\omega_n,\delta_n)\to \mathcal P(m_*,\kappa_* )\neq 0,
\qquad
\kappa_*:=\lim \frac{2\omega_n}{\delta_n}
\]
after passing to a subsequence. By swap symmetry, this profile is projective and even. This is the minimal surviving local obstruction if the analytic/quadratic harmlessness route fails. The summaries already isolate exactly this kind of alternative: any remaining obstruction must lie beyond the whole analytic swap-invariant quadratic layer. turn65file1

So the question becomes:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Can a nonzero subquadratic projective profile coexist with the cubic/quintic one-pair good-patch geometry?}
}
\]

## 2. Why the first bad profile should be impossible on a good patch

The key structural fact from the earlier handback is that on a good patch the one-pair cubic/quintic geometry is transverse:
\[
M=c(A_5^{\mathfrak f})'-c' A_5^{\mathfrak f}\neq 0.
\]
Equivalently, \((c,A_5^{\mathfrak f})\) and its derivative are linearly independent there. This is exactly what made the cubic-killing direction unique and the quintic value uniformly separated from zero in the blow-up model. 

That suggests the following contradiction strategy.

If a minimal nontrivial projective profile \(\mathcal P(m,\kappa)\) survives, then after dividing by the correct subquadratic scale it should define a genuine **projective-direction witness** on the blow-up sphere. But on a good patch, the only projective direction singled out by cubic cancellation is the canonical one
\[
\Theta_m^{\mathrm{can}}=c'(m)D_m-c(m)D_m',
\]
and along that direction the quintic model is forced to equal
\[
-\,M(m)\neq 0.
\]
So any actual bad branch would have to do one of two things:

- either converge to a direction different from the cubic-cancelling one, in which case cubic does not cancel and there is no bad branch;
- or converge to the cubic-cancelling direction, in which case quintic stays separated from zero by the \(M\)-gap, so again there is no bad branch. 

This is not yet a proof, because it uses the blow-up functoriality model for cubic/quintic. But it shows something important: **any subquadratic profile must somehow evade the ordinary projective cubic/quintic direction law**. So the first surviving profile cannot be just another honest projective-direction scalar built from the same one-pair geometry. It has to be more singular than that.

That is already a substantial narrowing.

## 3. Stronger fork: either quadratic boundedness, or genuinely nonlocal/provenance-sensitive singularity

Combine the new summaries:

- any analytic swap-invariant local scalar is automatically quadratic in the cancellation variables;
- on the involutive exact fixed-shear branch, even the whole finite descended transport package is quotient-visible and rank-one on the quartic–sextic rung;
- hence any still-live obstruction cannot come from ordinary analytic local dependence on the cancellation variables, amplitude ratio, and finite descended transport state. turn65file1

So the next sharpened dichotomy is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Either the actual defects are quadratically bounded, or the first surviving obstruction is \emph{not} an ordinary local scalar at all.}
}
\]

More concretely, if quadratic boundedness fails, then the surviving profile must be one of these:

1. **non-analytic in the projective slope** \(\kappa\);
2. **nonlocal in the branch parameter**, not determined by finitely many local quantities;
3. **provenance-sensitive/discrete**, meaning it depends on extra two-atom package data not visible in the local chart;
4. or tied to the stronger global quotient-septic / collision-functoriality lane. 

That is stronger than just saying “the corner remains open.” It says the remaining obstruction class is now extremely exotic.

## 4. A concrete theorem to attack next

The cleanest next theorem is a weak version of analyticity that is still enough:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{No subquadratic profile theorem on good patches.}
}
\]

For each corrected cubic/quintic defect \(E_j\), \(j=3,5\), and each compact good patch \(J\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\}\), there exists \(C_J\) such that
\[
|E_j(m,\omega,\delta)|\le C_J\bigl(\omega^2+|\omega\delta|+\delta^2\bigr)
\]
for all \((m,\omega,\delta)\) near \((J,0,0)\).

This is weaker than full analytic extension and weaker than the full normal-form statement, but it is exactly enough for the good-patch exclusion mechanism. If this holds, then along the involutive branch
\[
E_j=O((h_1-h_2)^2),
\]
and the local exact fixed-shear corner is excluded on good patches. This matches the closure mechanism already spelled out in the summaries. turn65file1

## 5. How I would try to prove it

I would now attack term-by-term.

Take the actual formula for the corrected cubic/quintic defects and separate it into:

- raw two-atom algebraic combinations of \(a_1,a_2,h_1,h_2\);
- normalization/whitening denominators;
- reparametrization corrections.

Then:

1. Rewrite everything in \((m,\Lambda,\delta)\), or better \((m,\omega,\delta)\).
2. Track the order of every numerator and denominator as \((\omega,\delta)\to (0,0)\).
3. Use the cancellation identity \(a_1c(h_1)+a_2c(h_2)\approx 0\) and swap symmetry to show that every would-be pole cancels to at least first order.
4. Then use the parity/swap argument to kill the entire first-order layer, forcing quadratic boundedness.

This is now the sharpest local attack because it avoids having to prove the whole package is analytic in one shot. It only asks for the exact amount of regularity needed for exclusion.

## 6. What this says about septic

This attack also pushes order \(7\) further out of the local picture.

On good patches, if the no-subquadratic-profile theorem holds, then cubic/quintic already kill close cancelling bad cores. So the quotient-septic class
\[
[A_7^{\mathfrak f}] \in \mathfrak f/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\]
is not the first local obstruction there. It only remains relevant for the stronger global route: same reduced image germ, collision functoriality, or whatever genuinely provenance-sensitive datum survives after all lower local analytic structure has been exhausted. That is fully consistent with the summaries. 

## Bottom line

The attack has now sharpened to this:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Prove quadratic boundedness on the cancellation chart, or else identify the first genuinely non-analytic projective blow-up profile.}
}
\]

And the second option is already so exotic that I suspect the first is the right theorem.

So the next theorem I would try to prove is exactly:

\[
\boxed{
|E_{12}^{(j)}(m,\omega,\delta)|\lesssim \omega^2+|\omega\delta|+\delta^2
\quad (j=3,5)
}
\]

on compact good patches. If that lands, the good-patch local two-point lane is essentially over.

_Thought for 18s_

Here is the next honest push.

I think the attack has now reduced to a very sharp **minimal bad profile problem**, and that gives a stronger theorem target than before.

The summaries already imply this fork on a compact good patch
\[
J\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\},\qquad
M:=c(A_5^{\mathfrak f})'-c'A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

Either the corrected cubic/quintic defects are quadratically bounded on the cancellation chart, in which case the local exact fixed-shear lane dies, or there is a first surviving **subquadratic projective blow-up profile**. turn65file1

So let me attack the second possibility directly.

## 1. Minimal bad profile formulation

Write a corrected defect as
\[
E(m,\omega,\delta),
\]
with cancellation variables
\[
m=\frac{h_1+h_2}{2},\qquad
\delta=h_2-h_1,\qquad
\omega=\frac{\Lambda-1}{\Lambda+1},\qquad
\Lambda=-\frac{a_2}{a_1}.
\]
Under atom swap,
\[
(m,\omega,\delta)\mapsto(m,-\omega,-\delta).
\]

Assume quadratic boundedness fails. Then there should exist a smallest exponent
\[
\alpha<2
\]
and a blow-up sequence
\[
(m_n,\omega_n,\delta_n)\to(m_*,0,0),\qquad
\rho_n:=|\omega_n|+|\delta_n|\to 0,
\]
for which
\[
\rho_n^{-\alpha}E(m_n,\omega_n,\delta_n)\to \mathcal P(m_*,\kappa_* )\neq 0,
\qquad
\kappa_*:=\lim \frac{2\omega_n}{\delta_n},
\]
after passing to a subsequence.

That \(\mathcal P\) is the first surviving local obstruction. By the swap symmetry already built into the chart, it cannot be an ordinary odd linear tangent-direction term. So the first bad profile is automatically more rigid than a generic first-order blow-up law. This matches the summary’s conclusion that the entire linear blown-up layer is already dead. 

## 2. What such a profile would have to do on a genuine bad branch

A true close bad branch does not just produce one defect. It forces simultaneous smallness/vanishing of the corrected cubic and quintic defects. So if a subquadratic obstruction exists, there should be profiles
\[
\mathcal P_3(m,\kappa),\qquad \mathcal P_5(m,\kappa)
\]
with a common zero at the limiting projective direction:
\[
\mathcal P_3(m_*,\kappa_*)=0,\qquad \mathcal P_5(m_*,\kappa_*)=0.
\]

That is the key extra restriction. It is not enough for one profile to survive; a bad branch must survive the cubic and quintic tests together.

Now compare this with the one-pair good-patch geometry already isolated earlier. If the first surviving blow-up layer is functorial in the projective source direction
\[
\Theta_{m,\theta}=\cos\theta\,D_m+\sin\theta\,D_m',
\qquad
\kappa=2\cot\theta,
\]
then the model cubic/quintic profiles are
\[
C(m,\theta)=\cos\theta\,c(m)+\sin\theta\,c'(m),
\]
\[
K(m,\theta)=\cos\theta\,A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)+\sin\theta\,(A_5^{\mathfrak f})'(m).
\]
On a good patch, \(C=0\) determines a unique direction, and at that direction
\[
K=-\,\frac{M}{\sqrt{c^2+(c')^2}}\neq 0.
\]
So any actual minimal bad profile must **fail** to be just the one-pair projective law. If it were the ordinary projective law, good-patch transversality would already kill it. 

This is an important sharpening:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Any first surviving bad profile must already lie beyond the ordinary one-pair projective cubic/quintic law.}
}
\]

So the remaining obstruction, if any, is not merely “projective.” It has to be a projective profile carrying genuinely extra two-atom/package information.

## 3. Stronger reduction: the first surviving obstruction must be a relational profile

Combining the new summaries with the earlier transport descent gives a very clean frontier.

The obstruction cannot come from:
- the finite descended transport state,
- any finite analytic swap-invariant local scalar built from the cancellation variables and that state,
- or the ordinary one-pair projective tangent family. turn65file1

Therefore the first surviving local obstruction, if it exists, must be a **relational profile**
\[
\mathcal R(m,\kappa)
\]
that is not reducible to either:
1. a function of the one-pair data at \(m\), or
2. a function of the quotient-visible transport scalar \(Q\).

In other words,

\[
\boxed{
\text{the first possible local obstruction is already the first genuinely relational two-atom blow-up invariant.}
}
\]

That is stronger than anything we had before. It says the geometry and all local analytic scalar structure have already been exhausted.

## 4. The next theorem to attack

So the next theorem target is no longer just quadratic boundedness. It is this dichotomy:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Relational-profile dichotomy on good patches.}
}
\]

On a compact good patch \(J\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\}\), either

1. the corrected cubic/quintic defects are quadratically bounded in the cancellation variables, hence harmless; or

2. there exists a first nontrivial subquadratic **relational** projective profile
   \[
   (\mathcal R_3,\mathcal R_5)(m,\kappa)
   \]
   with a common zero.

And if you can rule out such relational profiles, the local lane is finished.

That is the right formulation because it isolates exactly what remains after all the universal analytic structure has been stripped away.

## 5. Why I think the relational profile should also fail

Here is the heuristic reason.

The summaries on the exact fixed-shear corner say that even the whole finite transport state is quotient-visible and rank-one on the quartic–sextic rung. So any relational profile that still survives cannot be assembled from finitely many descended one-atom states. It must come from some more exotic package-level dependence. But near cancellation, the only first-order source datum is already the single projective direction
\[
\Theta_{m,\theta}.
\]
So a local relational profile would have to assign extra invariant information to that same first-order direction.

That looks implausible unless the corrected package is genuinely non-analytic or carries hidden discrete/provenance data across collision. And that is exactly the exotic frontier the summaries already identify. 

So my working conjecture is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{No subquadratic relational projective profile exists on }J\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\}.
}
\]

Proving that would finish the good-patch local lane even without first proving full analytic extension.

## 6. Concrete proof strategy from here

There are now two viable next attacks.

The cleaner one is still:

\[
|E_{12}^{(j)}(m,\omega,\delta)|\lesssim \omega^2+|\omega\delta|+\delta^2,\qquad j=3,5,
\]
on compact good patches. That kills every subquadratic profile at once.

But the more conceptual one is:

- define the minimal blow-up exponent \(\alpha_j\) for each defect,
- show any corresponding profile must be projective,
- show any projective profile compatible with a bad branch must be relational,
- then show no such relational profile can arise from the corrected package on a good patch.

That second route is messier, but it gives a more structural contradiction if it lands.

## 7. The best immediate mathematical takeaway

So the attack has now sharpened to:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The remaining local two-point problem is no longer geometric. It is the question of whether a first genuinely relational projective blow-up profile can survive on the cancellation chart.}
}
\]

And I think the next theorem to prove is still the quadratic boundedness one, because it is the shortest route to killing that possibility.

But conceptually, the current frontier is now much clearer:

- universal local analytic scalar structure is dead,
- ordinary projective one-pair geometry is dead,
- finite descended transport-state mechanisms are dead,
- so any still-live obstruction would have to be the first genuinely relational/projective package-level profile.

That is the strongest local compression I can honestly claim right now.
