_Thought for 7s_

Here is the next real attack.

I am going to push the endpoint-opposition bridge in a more rigorous local form, using inward endpoint coordinates and a one-sided fold inversion lemma. That is the right next theorem to try to land now that the regime has been corrected to the genuine overlap case. 【225†source】【226†source】

## 1. The theorem to prove

Assume we are in the open-overlap regime
\[
B_0+B_2>B_1,
\]
so the two outer runs admit a nontrivial common value interval
\[
I=[q_-,q_+]
\]
with inverse branches
\[
\phi_0,\phi_2,
\qquad
\widehat Q(\phi_i(q))=q,
\]
and branch gap
\[
\Delta(q):=\phi_2(q)-\phi_0(q)>0.
\]

The theorem I want is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Endpoint-opposition theorem. }
\Delta'(q_-^+)\text{ and }\Delta'(q_+^-)\text{ have opposite signs.}
}
\]

Then there exists
\[
q_*\in(q_-,q_+)
\]
with
\[
\Delta'(q_*)=0,
\]
so overlap produces an interior same-value / same-\(J_1\) witness.

## 2. Reduce to a local one-sided fold lemma

At \(q_-\), exactly one outer branch is singular. Say it is \(\phi_0\), meeting a one-sided scalar fold at \(u=u_-\). Introduce the inward value coordinate
\[
\eta_-:=q-q_-\ge 0.
\]
Locally,
\[
\widehat Q(u)=q_-+\sigma_-(u-u_-)^{m_-}+O((u-u_-)^{m_-+1}),
\qquad
m_-\ge 2,\ \sigma_-\neq 0.
\]
On the relevant one-sided inverse branch,
\[
u-u_- \sim c_-\,\eta_-^{1/m_-},
\]
so
\[
\frac{d\phi_0}{d\eta_-} \sim \frac{c_-}{m_-}\,\eta_-^{-(m_--1)/m_-}.
\]
This has a definite sign, namely \(\operatorname{sgn}(c_-)\).

Likewise at \(q_+\), exactly one outer branch is singular. Say it is \(\phi_2\), meeting a one-sided scalar fold at \(u=u_+\). Introduce the inward coordinate from the right
\[
\eta_+:=q_+-q\ge 0.
\]
Locally,
\[
\widehat Q(u)=q_+-\sigma_+(u-u_+)^{m_+}+O((u-u_+)^{m_++1}),
\qquad
m_+\ge 2,\ \sigma_+\neq 0,
\]
on the relevant inward side. Then
\[
u-u_+ \sim c_+\,\eta_+^{1/m_+},
\]
so
\[
\frac{d\phi_2}{d\eta_+} \sim \frac{c_+}{m_+}\,\eta_+^{-(m_+-1)/m_+}.
\]
Again this has definite sign \(\operatorname{sgn}(c_+)\).

So the key local lemma becomes:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{One-sided fold sign lemma. }
\text{The inward singular inverse derivatives at the two overlap endpoints have the same sign: }
\operatorname{sgn}\frac{d\phi_0}{d\eta_-}(0^+)
=
\operatorname{sgn}\frac{d\phi_2}{d\eta_+}(0^+).
}
\]

If that lemma holds, the endpoint-opposition theorem follows immediately.

## 3. Why the inward signs should match

This is the local geometric point.

Both \(\phi_0\) at the left end and \(\phi_2\) at the right end are the branches that move **into the overlap interval** as the inward parameter increases from \(0\). They are the two inward-pointing endpoint shells of the same overlap interval.

So relative to the inward orientation, they are the same kind of one-sided inverse branch: each is the branch that enters the common value range from its endpoint fold. There is no sign flip between them at the level of inward parameters. Thus their inward singular inverse derivatives should have the same sign.

Now convert back to derivatives with respect to \(q\). Since
\[
\eta_-=q-q_-,
\qquad
\eta_+=q_+-q,
\]
we have
\[
\frac{d\phi_0}{dq}=\frac{d\phi_0}{d\eta_-},
\qquad
\frac{d\phi_2}{dq}=-\frac{d\phi_2}{d\eta_+}.
\]
Therefore
\[
\operatorname{sgn}\phi_0'(q_-^+)
=
\operatorname{sgn}\frac{d\phi_0}{d\eta_-}(0^+),
\qquad
\operatorname{sgn}\phi_2'(q_+^-)
=
-\operatorname{sgn}\frac{d\phi_2}{d\eta_+}(0^+).
\]
If the inward signs match, then
\[
\operatorname{sgn}\phi_2'(q_+^-)
=
-\operatorname{sgn}\phi_0'(q_-^+).
\]

Now use
\[
\Delta'(q)=\phi_2'(q)-\phi_0'(q).
\]
Near \(q_-\), \(\phi_0'\) is singular and \(\phi_2'\) is finite, so
\[
\operatorname{sgn}\Delta'(q_-^+)=-\operatorname{sgn}\phi_0'(q_-^+).
\]
Near \(q_+\), \(\phi_2'\) is singular and \(\phi_0'\) is finite, so
\[
\operatorname{sgn}\Delta'(q_+^-)=\operatorname{sgn}\phi_2'(q_+^-).
\]
Combining these,
\[
\operatorname{sgn}\Delta'(q_+^-)
=
-\operatorname{sgn}\phi_0'(q_-^+)
=
\operatorname{sgn}\Delta'(q_-^+) \cdot (-1).
\]
Hence endpoint-opposition.

So the whole theorem reduces to the inward one-sided fold sign lemma.

## 4. Consequence: interior witness exists

Once endpoint-opposition is in hand,
\[
\operatorname{sgn}\Delta'(q_-^+)=-\operatorname{sgn}\Delta'(q_+^-)
\]
implies there is some
\[
q_*\in(q_-,q_+)
\]
with
\[
\Delta'(q_*)=0.
\]

But
\[
\phi_i'(q)=J_1(\phi_i(q)),
\qquad
J_1(u)=\frac{1}{\widehat Q'(u)},
\]
so at \(q_*\),
\[
J_1(\phi_0(q_*))=J_1(\phi_2(q_*)),
\]
and of course
\[
\widehat Q(\phi_0(q_*))=\widehat Q(\phi_2(q_*))=q_*.
\]

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
B_0+B_2>B_1
\Longrightarrow
\exists q_*\in(q_-,q_+):
(\widehat Q,J_1)(\phi_0(q_*))=(\widehat Q,J_1)(\phi_2(q_*)).
}
\]

That is the corrected overlap-to-transport bridge.

## 5. The next attack after that

Once the witness exists, the next theorem remains the first closure checkpoint:
\[
\boxed{
(\widehat Q,J_1)\text{ same at an outer witness}
\Longrightarrow
J_2\text{ same there.}
}
\]
Since
\[
J_2(u)=J_1(u)\partial_u J_1(u)
=
-\,\frac{\widehat Q''(u)}{(\widehat Q'(u))^3}
=-\Xi(u),
\]
this is witness-level \(\Xi\)-descent.

If it holds, then
\[
\delta J_2(q_*)=0,
\]
so the witness is already more degenerate than a first-order live crossing, and the higher reciprocal-slope tower comes online. If it fails, that failure is already the first explicit nonlocal transport obstruction. 【226†source】

## 6. The most specific next sub-attack

So the next thing I would try to formalize is exactly this lemma:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{For the two inward-pointing endpoint shells of a nontrivial overlap interval, the inward singular inverse derivatives have the same sign.}
}
\]

Once that is written cleanly, the endpoint-opposition theorem is basically done, and the transport tower attack can finally run in the correct regime.

_Thought for 7s_

Here is the next real attack.

I think the best way to stop hand-waving around the endpoint-opposition lemma is to replace it with a more invariant statement that does not depend on guessing singular signs by eye.

The right object is not \(\phi_0'\) and \(\phi_2'\) separately, but the **oriented entry map** of the overlap interval.

## 1. Repackage the overlap bridge

We are in the genuine outer-overlap regime
\[
B_0+B_2>B_1,
\]
so there is a nontrivial common value interval
\[
I=[q_-,q_+]
\]
for the two outer runs, with inverse branches
\[
\phi_0,\phi_2,
\qquad
\widehat Q(\phi_i(q))=q,
\]
and branch gap
\[
\Delta(q)=\phi_2(q)-\phi_0(q)>0.
\]

The theorem I need is still:

\[
\boxed{
\text{There exists }q_*\in(q_-,q_+)\text{ with }\Delta'(q_*)=0.
}
\]

But I now think the cleanest route is not “endpoint singularities have opposite signs,” but:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{The gap }\Delta\textbf{ cannot be strictly monotone on a maximal overlap interval.}
}
\]

That is weaker than explicit endpoint-opposition, but it is enough.

## 2. Why strict monotonicity of \(\Delta\) should be impossible

A maximal overlap interval has two different boundary mechanisms:

- at \(q_-\), the left outer branch is the one that dies;
- at \(q_+\), the right outer branch is the one that dies.

So the overlap interval is born by one shell at the left end and dies by the other shell at the right end. This asymmetry already fights strict monotonicity of the shell-gap.

If \(\Delta\) were strictly monotone on all of \(I\), then one of two things would happen:

- either the gap is always shrinking as \(q\) runs through the interval;
- or it is always expanding.

But a strictly shrinking gap would mean the dominant endpoint geometry at both ends is controlled by the same side of the two-shell configuration, and a strictly expanding gap would mean the opposite. Neither matches the actual boundary-pinching picture, where the left endpoint is controlled by one shell and the right endpoint by the other.

So the structural theorem I would now try to prove is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{On a maximal common value interval of two outer shells, the branch-gap }\Delta
\textbf{ cannot be globally one-sided monotone.}
}
\]

That immediately yields an interior extremum.

This is better than my earlier endpoint-sign theorem because it avoids needing the full sign bookkeeping right away.

## 3. A local proof strategy for non-monotonicity

I would try to prove it as follows.

Near \(q_-\), exactly one branch is singular. Say \(\phi_0\). Then
\[
\Delta'(q)=\phi_2'(q)-\phi_0'(q)
\]
is dominated by \(-\phi_0'(q)\).

Near \(q_+\), exactly one branch is singular. Say \(\phi_2\). Then
\[
\Delta'(q)
\]
is dominated by \(+\phi_2'(q)\).

So the only way \(\Delta\) could be strictly monotone on all of \(I\) is if those two singular contributions had the same sign effect on \(\Delta'\). But because they come from different shells and enter the overlap interval from opposite ends, the sign effects are geometrically incompatible.

So the most local intermediate lemma is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{The singular shell controlling }q_-\textbf{ and the singular shell controlling }q_+\textbf{ contribute opposite effects to }\Delta'.}
}
\]

That is really the content I need. Once that is proved, strict monotonicity of \(\Delta\) is impossible.

## 4. What this gives immediately

Then there exists \(q_*\in(q_-,q_+)\) such that
\[
\Delta'(q_*)=0.
\]

But
\[
\phi_i'(q)=J_1(\phi_i(q)),
\qquad
J_1(u)=\frac1{\widehat Q'(u)},
\]
so
\[
J_1(\phi_0(q_*))=J_1(\phi_2(q_*)),
\]
and of course
\[
\widehat Q(\phi_0(q_*))=\widehat Q(\phi_2(q_*))=q_*.
\]

So overlap yields the exact transport witness we want:

\[
\boxed{
B_0+B_2>B_1
\Longrightarrow
\exists q_*\in(q_-,q_+):
(\widehat Q,J_1)(\phi_0(q_*))=(\widehat Q,J_1)(\phi_2(q_*)).
}
\]

That is the corrected bridge to the reciprocal-slope tower. This is exactly the regime correction your note imposed, and it matches the updated transport framing in the notes.【225†source】【226†source】

## 5. Then the real transport attack starts

Once such a witness exists, the next theorem remains:

\[
\boxed{
(\widehat Q,J_1)\text{ same at an outer witness}
\Longrightarrow
J_2\text{ same there.}
}
\]

Since
\[
J_{n+1}=J_1\partial_u J_n,
\qquad
J_2(u)=J_1(u)\partial_u J_1(u)
=
-\,\frac{\widehat Q''(u)}{(\widehat Q'(u))^3}
=-\Xi(u),
\]
this is witness-level \(\Xi\)-descent.

If it holds, then
\[
\delta J_2(q_*)=0,
\]
so the witness is already more degenerate than a first-order live crossing, and the higher \(J_n\)-tower becomes the right object. If it fails, that failure is already the first explicit nonlocal transport obstruction. That is fully aligned with the updated notes’ fork.【226†source】

## 6. So the sharpened attack is now

The next specific theorem I would try to prove is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{On a maximal outer-overlap interval, the branch-gap }\Delta\textbf{ is not strictly monotone.}
}
\]

That is enough to produce the interior witness and turn on the actual transport-tower endgame in the correct regime.

After that, the next attack is still witness-set first-order closure:
\[
(\widehat Q,J_1)\Rightarrow J_2.
\]

That is the cleanest continuation I see right now.

## Assistant (2026-04-22 02:20:33)

_Thought for 9s_

Here is the next real attack.

I think the best way to move this from heuristic to something checkable is to **replace the global monotonicity claim for \(\Delta\)** with a much more local, more plausible statement:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{On a maximal outer-overlap interval, }\Delta\textbf{ has opposite one-sided derivative signs at the two boundary pinches.}
}
\]

That is enough. I do not need a global theorem first.

The updated notes make clear that the \(\Delta/\Xi/J_n\) transport story belongs only in the actual overlap regime
\[
B_0+B_2>B_1,
\]
so the task is now to extract an interior witness from that overlap, then start the transport-tower closure test.【225†source】【226†source】

## 1. Set up the exact local problem

Let
\[
I=[q_-,q_+]
\]
be the maximal common value interval of the two outer runs, with inverse branches
\[
\phi_0,\phi_2,
\qquad
\widehat Q(\phi_i(q))=q,
\]
and gap
\[
\Delta(q)=\phi_2(q)-\phi_0(q)>0.
\]

To get the transport witness I want to prove:
\[
\exists q_*\in(q_-,q_+)\quad \Delta'(q_*)=0.
\]

The clean route is to show:
\[
\operatorname{sgn}\Delta'(q_-^+)=-\operatorname{sgn}\Delta'(q_+^-).
\]

## 2. Reduce endpoint signs to one-sided fold inversions

At \(q_-\), exactly one outer branch dies. Say it is \(\phi_0\). The other, \(\phi_2\), is regular there. So near \(q_-\),
\[
\Delta'(q)=\phi_2'(q)-\phi_0'(q)
\]
is dominated by the singular inverse derivative of \(\phi_0\).

Similarly, at \(q_+\), exactly one outer branch dies. Say it is \(\phi_2\). Then near \(q_+\),
\[
\Delta'(q)
\]
is dominated by the singular inverse derivative of \(\phi_2\).

So the whole theorem reduces to a local sign comparison of the two singular inverse derivatives:
\[
\boxed{
\text{left pinch contributes }-\phi_0',\quad\text{right pinch contributes }+\phi_2'.
}
\]

Thus I only need:
\[
\operatorname{sgn}\phi_0'(q_-^+)=\operatorname{sgn}\phi_2'(q_+^-).
\]

## 3. The right local lemma

The local statement I would now try to prove is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Inward one-sided fold lemma.}
}
\]

Suppose \(q=q_c\) is a one-sided scalar fold endpoint for an inverse branch \(u=\phi(q)\), and parametrize values inward from the endpoint by
\[
\eta=\pm(q-q_c)\ge 0
\]
with the sign chosen so that \(\eta\) increases into the common value interval. Then the singular inverse derivative
\[
\frac{d\phi}{d\eta}
\]
has a definite sign determined only by the choice of the inward branch, not by whether the endpoint is left or right.

If that lemma is true, then the singular inward derivatives of the two boundary branches agree in sign, because both branches are exactly the inward-pointing shells of the same overlap interval. Converting back to \(d/dq\) introduces one minus sign on the right endpoint, and that produces endpoint-opposition for \(\Delta'\).

That is the correct local mechanism.

## 4. Why this lemma is plausible

Take the local fold normal form
\[
\widehat Q(u)=q_c+\sigma (u-u_c)^m+O((u-u_c)^{m+1}),
\qquad m\ge 2,\ \sigma\neq 0.
\]
On a chosen one-sided inverse branch,
\[
u-u_c\sim c\,\eta^{1/m},
\]
so
\[
\frac{d\phi}{d\eta}\sim \frac{c}{m}\,\eta^{-(m-1)/m}.
\]

The sign is just \(\operatorname{sgn}(c)\), i.e. the sign of the chosen one-sided branch in the \(u\)-coordinate. For the two outer shells bounding a common overlap interval, the inward-pointing branch on the left and the inward-pointing branch on the right are the same geometric type: both are the shell that enters the overlap set as the inward parameter increases. So they should have the same sign in inward coordinates.

That gives:
\[
\operatorname{sgn}\frac{d\phi_0}{d\eta_-}(0^+)
=
\operatorname{sgn}\frac{d\phi_2}{d\eta_+}(0^+),
\]
where
\[
\eta_-=q-q_-,
\qquad
\eta_+=q_+-q.
\]

Then
\[
\phi_0'(q)=\frac{d\phi_0}{d\eta_-},
\qquad
\phi_2'(q)=-\frac{d\phi_2}{d\eta_+},
\]
so
\[
\operatorname{sgn}\phi_2'(q_+^-)
=
-\operatorname{sgn}\phi_0'(q_-^+).
\]

Since \(\Delta'\sim-\phi_0'\) at the left end and \(\Delta'\sim+\phi_2'\) at the right end, this yields
\[
\operatorname{sgn}\Delta'(q_-^+)=-\operatorname{sgn}\Delta'(q_+^-).
\]

That is the endpoint-opposition theorem.

## 5. Consequence: interior witness in the correct regime

Once endpoint-opposition is established,
\[
\exists q_*\in(q_-,q_+)\quad \Delta'(q_*)=0.
\]

But
\[
\phi_i'(q)=J_1(\phi_i(q)),
\qquad
J_1(u)=\frac{1}{\widehat Q'(u)},
\]
so at \(q_*\),
\[
J_1(\phi_0(q_*))=J_1(\phi_2(q_*)),
\]
and of course
\[
\widehat Q(\phi_0(q_*))=\widehat Q(\phi_2(q_*))=q_*.
\]

So I get the exact corrected bridge:
\[
\boxed{
B_0+B_2>B_1
\Longrightarrow
\exists q_*\in(q_-,q_+):
(\widehat Q,J_1)(\phi_0(q_*))=(\widehat Q,J_1)(\phi_2(q_*)).
}
\]

That is precisely the overlap-to-transport witness needed for the rest of the endgame. It is also exactly the regime correction your note imposed. 【225†source】【226†source】

## 6. Then the next theorem is finally clean

Once that witness exists, the next attack is no longer vague at all. It is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Witness-set first-order closure: }
(\widehat Q,J_1)\textbf{ determines }J_2.
}
\]

Equivalently, on outer witness pairs,
\[
\widehat Q(u_0)=\widehat Q(u_2),\quad
J_1(u_0)=J_1(u_2)
\Longrightarrow
J_2(u_0)=J_2(u_2).
\]

Since
\[
J_2(u)=J_1(u)\partial_u J_1(u)
=
-\,\frac{\widehat Q''(u)}{(\widehat Q'(u))^3}
=-\Xi(u),
\]
this is exactly witness-level \(\Xi\)-descent.

If that holds, then
\[
\delta J_2(q_*)=0,
\]
and the witness is already more degenerate than a first-order live crossing. Then the higher reciprocal-slope tower
\[
J_{n+1}=J_1\partial_u J_n
\]
comes online, and one can try to force touching / translated replication. If it fails, that failure is already the first explicit nonlocal transport obstruction. 【226†source】

## 7. The exact next sub-attack

So the next proof attempt I would make is:

1. Formalize the one-sided fold inversion lemma in inward endpoint coordinates.
2. Deduce endpoint-opposition for \(\Delta'\).
3. Extract the interior same-value / same-\(J_1\) witness.
4. Immediately test witness-level first-order closure
   \[
   (\widehat Q,J_1)\Rightarrow J_2.
   \]

That is now the sharpest attack path.

## Assistant (2026-04-22 02:56:37)

_Thought for 25s_

Yes. Here is the full recap of my attack, restricted to the material that is **not yet in the paper** or is only partially reflected there, with the current status separated into: structural gains, concrete theorem targets, negative findings, and speculative bridges.

The shortest honest summary is this: my attack did not produce a final closure, but it did push the remaining burden into a much narrower and cleaner shape. The big change is that the live problem now looks much less like “find one more local geometric contradiction” and much more like a small number of explicit transport / package-level closure problems. That picture is consistent with the latest consolidated notes, especially the three-front compression, the corrected overlap/separation trichotomy, and the package-level ceiling on new pointwise generators.【225†source】【226†source】

## 1. The overall compression I arrived at

The attack now sees three narrow fronts.

On the **nonmixed/global affine** side, the remaining burden is no longer vague recurrence but RH-specific exclusion of remote endpoint-gap zeros. Pure affine / pseudoline / interval-graph geometry has hit a real ceiling. Any further progress there has to come from source structure, not more naked plane-curve geometry. This matches the latest notes, but one of my contributions was to stop trying to squeeze that lane geometrically and instead treat the affine ceiling as real, not provisional.【225†source】

On the **mixed exact fixed-shear** side, the live residual geometry has compressed to the quotient-visible one-variable transport problem, but with an important correction: the inverse-branch-gap / \(\Delta\) / \(\Xi\) transport setup only belongs in the genuine overlap regime
\[
B_0+B_2>B_1,
\]
not in the separation regime
\[
B_1>B_0+B_2.
\]
That correction was crucial. It means all the outer inverse-branch transport analysis must be understood as **conditional on actual outer overlap**. Once that is imposed, the right task is to produce an interior witness from overlap and then run the transport-tower closure test.【225†source】

On the **honest order-7 / package** side, my attack increasingly treats the real target as a closure/functoriality theorem — same reduced image germ at coincidence, collision-functoriality, or equivalent package-level closure — not raw septic equality. The generator audit is now decisive here: no second explicit pointwise highest-new generator has appeared beyond the current septic direction, so if anything survives, it is likely transport/global/package-level rather than another local scalar field.【225†source】【226†source】

That three-front architecture is partially in the notes, but what I added was a fairly systematic attempt to align all later attacks with it and stop pursuing lanes that had already hit a ceiling.

## 2. The corrected fixed-shear transport program

This is where most of my new work went.

### 2.1 The first correction: the overlap regime was misidentified

A key correction was that I initially treated
\[
B_1>B_0+B_2
\]
as the live overlap case. That was wrong. The correct trichotomy is:

\[
B_0+B_2>B_1 \quad\text{open outer overlap,}
\]
\[
B_0+B_2=B_1 \quad\text{touching,}
\]
\[
B_1>B_0+B_2 \quad\text{separation.}
\]

So the inverse-branch-gap machinery belongs only to
\[
B_0+B_2>B_1.
\]

This correction does not damage the transport identities themselves, but it does completely change the logical order of attack: first prove overlap gives an interior witness, then run the \(J_n\)-tower. That corrected organization is one of the most important things I learned that was not in the older draft logic.【225†source】

### 2.2 The correct bridge theorem now needed

Once the regime is corrected, the first theorem needed on that lane is no longer “strict excess implies a witness.” It is:

\[
\boxed{
B_0+B_2>B_1
\Longrightarrow
\exists q_*\in(q_-,q_+)\text{ with }\Delta'(q_*)=0.
}
\]

Here \(I=[q_-,q_+]\) is the common value interval of the two outer runs, \(\phi_0,\phi_2\) are the outer inverse branches, and
\[
\Delta(q)=\phi_2(q)-\phi_0(q).
\]

This is the **overlap-to-witness bridge**. It is not yet in theorem form in the paper.

### 2.3 My main new attack on that bridge: endpoint-opposition / non-monotonicity of the gap

I then tried to reduce the overlap-to-witness bridge to a local endpoint statement. The cleanest version I found is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{On a maximal outer-overlap interval, }\Delta\text{ cannot be strictly monotone.}
}
\]

A stronger version is the **endpoint-opposition theorem**:
\[
\operatorname{sgn}\Delta'(q_-^+)=-\operatorname{sgn}\Delta'(q_+^-).
\]

If that holds, then by continuity \(\Delta'\) has an interior zero, giving the desired witness.

The reasoning is local and geometric. At \(q_-\), exactly one outer branch becomes singular; at \(q_+\), the other outer branch becomes singular. So the two ends of the overlap interval are controlled by different boundary-pinching events. My attack was to formalize this via one-sided scalar fold inversion asymptotics, using inward endpoint coordinates:
\[
\eta_-=q-q_-,
\qquad
\eta_+=q_+-q.
\]

This led to the local theorem target:

\[
\boxed{
\text{For the two inward-pointing endpoint shells of a nontrivial overlap interval, the inward singular inverse derivatives have the same sign.}
}
\]

From that one gets endpoint-opposition for \(\Delta'\).

I do **not** claim this is proved. But it is the cleanest local theorem target I found for activating the transport lane in the correct regime.

### 2.4 Once a witness exists, the right object is the reciprocal-slope tower

Once \(q_*\) exists with \(\Delta'(q_*)=0\), one gets a same-value / same-\(J_1\) witness:
\[
\widehat Q(\phi_0(q_*))=\widehat Q(\phi_2(q_*))=q_*,
\qquad
J_1(\phi_0(q_*))=J_1(\phi_2(q_*)),
\qquad
J_1(u)=\frac1{\widehat Q'(u)}.
\]

I then introduced the full reciprocal-slope tower
\[
J_{n+1}(u):=J_1(u)\,\partial_u J_n(u),
\qquad
\delta J_n(q):=J_n(\phi_2(q))-J_n(\phi_0(q)).
\]

The exact transport identity is:
\[
\boxed{
\delta J_n'(q)=\delta J_{n+1}(q).
}
\]

This is one of the key “goodies” from my later attack. It means the Taylor series of the witness function
\[
\Delta'(q)=\delta J_1(q)
\]
at an interior witness \(q_*\) is controlled exactly term-by-term by the transported mismatch tower:
\[
\delta J_1(q)
=
\sum_{m\ge1}\frac{\delta J_{m+1}(q_*)}{m!}(q-q_*)^m.
\]

This turns the local type of the witness into a pure parity/closure question in the transported tower. I have not seen that exact formulation stated in the current draft.

### 2.5 The key parity insight

Let
\[
m_*:=\min\{n\ge 2:\delta J_n(q_*)\neq 0\}.
\]
Then locally
\[
\Delta'(q)
=
\frac{\delta J_{m_*}(q_*)}{(m_*-1)!}(q-q_*)^{m_*-1}
+ o((q-q_*)^{m_*-1}).
\]

So:

- if \(m_*\) is **even**, then \(m_*-1\) is odd, so \(\Delta'\) changes sign and \(q_*\) is a genuine extremum;
- if \(m_*\) is **odd**, then \(m_*-1\) is even, so \(\Delta'\) only touches zero.

This gave the clean parity target:

\[
\boxed{
\text{At any outer same-value / same-}J_1\text{ witness, the first nonzero transported mismatch should have touching parity.}
}
\]

This is not proved, but it is a very sharp reformulation of the transport lane that I do not think is yet properly in the paper.

### 2.6 The first closure checkpoint: witness-level \(\Xi\)-descent

Since
\[
J_2(u)=J_1(u)\partial_u J_1(u)
=
-\,\frac{\widehat Q''(u)}{(\widehat Q'(u))^3}
=-\Xi(u),
\]
the first closure checkpoint is:

\[
\boxed{
(\widehat Q,J_1)\text{ same at an outer witness}
\Longrightarrow
J_2\text{ same there.}
}
\]

Equivalently:

\[
\widehat Q(u_0)=\widehat Q(u_2),\quad J_1(u_0)=J_1(u_2)
\Longrightarrow
\Xi(u_0)=\Xi(u_2).
\]

This is the exact witness-level \(\Xi\)-descent statement.

If it holds, then
\[
\delta J_2(q_*)=0,
\]
so the witness is already more degenerate than a first-order crossing, and the tower is pushed up one level.

If it fails, then that failure is already the **first explicit nonlocal transport obstruction**.

That sharp fork — either witness-set closure holds and the witness becomes touching-like, or witness-set closure fails and the obstruction is explicitly nonlocal — is one of the cleanest new structural findings from my attack.

### 2.7 The stronger closure-law perspective

I then sharpened this one step more. Rather than only ask for \(\Xi\)-equality at witnesses, I reframed the problem as a **closure-law problem**:

\[
\boxed{
\text{On the outer witness set, }(\widehat Q,J_1)\text{ determines }J_2.
}
\]

This is weaker than asking for a global formula \(J_2=\mathcal G(\widehat Q,J_1)\) everywhere, but it is exactly what the witness set needs.

If this witness-set closure propagates upward,
\[
(\widehat Q,J_1)\Rightarrow J_2\Rightarrow J_3\Rightarrow\cdots,
\]
then same-value / same-\(J_1\) would force equality of the whole transported reciprocal-slope tower, and the only plausible global outcome would be the translated-replication / touching scenario already suggested in the notes:
\[
\Omega_0=\Omega_2,\qquad
B_0=B_2,\qquad
\phi_2(q)-\phi_0(q)\equiv C,\qquad
\widehat Q(u+C)=\widehat Q(u)\text{ on }R_0.
\]

So one big “goodie” is: the overlap-regime transport lane now has a very sharp fork.

Either:
- overlap \(\Rightarrow\) witness \(\Rightarrow\) witness-level closure \(\Rightarrow\) higher-order touching / translated replication,

or:
- witness-level closure fails, and that failure is already the first explicit nonlocal obstruction.

That is a much cleaner endgame than the earlier looser geometric story.

## 3. Other structural findings and no-gos from the later attack

### 3.1 I stopped treating pure affine geometry as a closure tool

On the nonmixed/global affine side, one thing I would now state firmly is: the universal affine/pseudoline ceiling is real. I no longer think more naked affine geometry is a productive closure route. The correct remaining task there is not “one more geometric lemma,” but an RH-specific / source-coupled obstruction to zeros of the remote endpoint-gap functions. That is more a strategic no-go than a theorem, but I think it is an important conclusion of the attack.

### 3.2 The local good-patch lane is increasingly package-level

On the good-patch / collision-cancellation side, the earlier attack led me to the **section-corrected quintic gap detector**
\[
\delta\Gamma_{(U,V)}
=
V(m,\theta_*(m))
-
\frac{\partial_\theta K(m,\theta_*(m))}{\partial_\theta C(m,\theta_*(m))}
\,U(m,\theta_*(m)).
\]

A same-order local compensator is exactly a deformation with
\[
\delta\Gamma=-\Gamma\neq 0.
\]

The main new insight here was the bridge conjecture:

- trivial directions (odd reparametrization, lower scalar/value gauge) should satisfy \(\delta\Gamma=0\);
- therefore any deformation with \(\delta\Gamma\neq 0\) is nontrivial in the reduced deformation quotient;
- and the first genuinely transverse class should already be quotient-septic-visible.

That gives the useful contrapositive:
\[
[A_7^{\mathfrak f}]=0
\Longrightarrow
\text{no same-order local compensator on any good patch.}
\]

This bridge is not yet proved, and I do **not** think it should be promoted as a theorem. But it is one of the clearest new ways I found to align the local good-patch lane with the honest order-7 package lane.

### 3.3 Explicit package dichotomy via the \(r\)-direction

Combining the generator audit with the section-corrected gap detector gave me a sharp explicit-package fork:

If the first explicit pointwise transverse quotient is truly one-dimensional and generated by the \(r=q^{(7)}\)-direction, then either:

- the \(r\)-direction is **gap-visible**, i.e. \(\delta\Gamma_r\neq 0\), in which case the explicit pointwise package unifies the local good-patch compensator and the quotient-septic obstruction; or

- the \(r\)-direction is **gap-invisible**, i.e. \(\delta\Gamma_r=0\), in which case the entire explicit pointwise package is invisible to the local good-patch detector, and any surviving local obstruction must already lie outside the explicit pointwise package, i.e. in nonlocal transport / provenance-sensitive structure.

That is a clean and, I think, genuinely useful dichotomy, though it remains conjectural.

## 4. Negative findings / ceilings I would now treat as stable

These are not all new, but they are things my attack reinforced enough that I would treat them as durable.

The naive source-summed corrected-block route should be considered dead as a way to prove the strong merger law.

No hidden finite-order reset or second finite local transport variable is going to rescue the exact fixed-shear corner.

The local analytic swap-invariant scalar layer on the collision-cancellation chart is dead; any genuinely live obstruction must lie beyond that whole layer.

No second explicit pointwise highest-new generator is emerging in the current package beyond the present septic direction.

Pure affine/pseudoline geometry on the nonmixed/global lane has reached its ceiling.

And, after the regime correction, the inverse-branch-gap / \(\Delta/\Xi/J_n\) transport machinery should **never again** be phrased as if it belongs to the separation case \(B_1>B_0+B_2\). It belongs only to the open-overlap case \(B_0+B_2>B_1\). That correction is stable and important.

## 5. The current best theorem targets from my attack

If I had to summarize the concrete theorem targets my attack produced, they are these.

First, on the overlap-regime fixed-shear lane:

\[
\boxed{
B_0+B_2>B_1
\Longrightarrow
\exists q_*\in(q_-,q_+):
(\widehat Q,J_1)(\phi_0(q_*))=(\widehat Q,J_1)(\phi_2(q_*)).
}
\]

This is the overlap-to-witness theorem, currently reducible to the endpoint-opposition / non-monotonicity of \(\Delta\).

Second, once a witness exists:

\[
\boxed{
(\widehat Q,J_1)\text{ same at an outer witness}
\Longrightarrow
J_2\text{ same there.}
}
\]

This is the first witness-level closure / \(\Xi\)-descent checkpoint.

Third, if closure propagates:

\[
\boxed{
(\widehat Q,J_1)\Rightarrow J_2\Rightarrow J_3\Rightarrow\cdots
\Longrightarrow
\text{touching / translated replication, not a genuinely live overlap obstruction.}
}
\]

Fourth, on the good-patch / package bridge:

\[
\boxed{
[A_7^{\mathfrak f}]=0
\Longrightarrow
\text{no same-order local compensator on a good patch.}
}
\]

This remains conjectural, but it is the cleanest local-to-global bridge I found.

## 6. Bottom line

The main thing my later attack added is not a final theorem, but a much sharper organization of the remaining burden.

The corrected overlap-regime fixed-shear lane is no longer “some transport issue.” It is now:

\[
\text{overlap } \Longrightarrow \text{ witness } \Longrightarrow \text{ witness-level closure or explicit nonlocal obstruction.}
\]

That is a major sharpening.

The nonmixed/global affine lane has a real ceiling; any further progress there has to be source-coupled.

The local good-patch lane increasingly looks like a package-level / quotient-septic visibility problem rather than a purely local geometric one.

And the explicit pointwise package either already carries the local obstruction through the \(r\)-direction, or it is invisible to the local detector and the live obstruction is already outside it.

That is the fullest honest recap I can give of the attack material that is not yet properly in the paper.
